The balance of 1 Uri of Prasadam remaining after issuing 1 Uri of Prasadam for the twelve Nirvaham of the Sthanattar from the donor's share of a quarter of the offered prasadam, being 1 Nali of the Tiruppalli-Eluchchi-Prasadam per day, 
together with the balance of the Atirasam remaining after issuing one Atirasam for the Nirvaham in the Padi (offered) on the seventh festival day, 
and the balance of the four Atirasam remaining after issuing nine Atirasam for the twelve Nirvaham out of (the donor's share of) the thirteen Atirasam for each Padi (offered) on the days of the Sri Jayanti, Vasanta Paurnami and Sri Rama Navami, 
at this rate, the respective balances of the offerings made to Alagiya-Singar, your Acharya Van Sathakopa-Jiyar and the successive line of his disciples shall receive on be- half of the workmen engaged in the cultivation of your Nandavanam. 
The balance of the Prasadam and Atirasam remaining after deducting the donor's share we shall be empowered to distribute during the forenoon Adaippu. 
In this manner shall (your charity) be extant through- out the succession of your descendants till the lasting of the moon and the sun. 
Thus has the temple-accountant Tiruninra-Ur-Udaiyan composed (this deed) with the consent of the Srivaishna- The protection of the Srivaishnavas (is sought) for 
these". 
From the above inscription, we learn that Sri Nara- simhaswamy, otherwise called Alagiya Singar, had been en- 
THE TEMPLE AND ITS SCULPTURES 
73 
shrined in the temple before the date of the inscription which has been worked out as the 15th June, 1493 A.D. It is also clear that this God obtained Tirupponakam for 30 days and Athirasapadi for 3 days on Sri Jayanthi, Vasan- tha Paurnami and Sri Rama Navami days. Athirasapadi was also offered during the seven days of Brahmotsavam. It is interesting also to note that this inscription mentions of Van-Sathakopa-Jiyar the founder of the Ahobala Mutt of Sri Vaishnavas. Another inscription found on the south wall of the first prakaram in Tirumalai temple reads as fol- lows:1 
"We shall also supply each day, along with the one Tiruvolakkam of Alagiya-Singar, for the 3 Matha Sesham to be offered to Periya-Perumal 
3 Marakkal of rice, and 
1 Ulakku and 1 Alakku of ghee, 2 Nali of rice for the Matrai, 
vegetables as a relish for the Dadhyodana-Sanshi and 1 Alakku of pepper or seasoning (for the same offering). 
Thus is (this) written up by the temple-accountant Tiruninra-Ur-Udaiyan with the permission of the Srivaish- 
navas". 
From this inscription, it is also obvious that the offer- ings to Alagiya Singar were actually made to the Lord of Tirumalai or Periyaperumal in the name of Alagiya Singar. This has been the practice in the temple. 
The innermost temple:-We now come to the innermost temple comprising of the Tirumamani mantapam, the Tiru- vilankoyil or the snapana mantapam which leads into the Garbha Griham through the Ramar Medai and the Sayana mantapam or Antharala mantapam. 
1. T. T. D. Epigraphical series, Vol. II, Inscriptions of Saluva 
Narasimha's time, p. 70. 
74 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
The Tirumamani mantapam:-As we enter the inner Gopuram and step into the Vimana Pradakshinam, we notice the Garuda shrine which is a part of the Tirumamani manta- pam. On the outer walls of the Garuda shrine is a figure of Lord Vishnu in the Sayana pose. The Garuda shrine is a crudely built structure which is located in the eastern portion of the Tirumamani mantapam, opposite the Bangaru Vakili or the Gate of Gold which forms the western end of the Tirumamani mantapam leading into the Tiruvilankoyil or snapana mantapam. The Tirumamani mantapam was origi- nally an open mantapam. It has however been closed now by putting up railings all around it. This mantapam houses in addition to the Garuda shrine the Hundi where pilgrims drop their devotional offerings and 'mudupus' to the Lord of Tirumalai. This Hundi is located on the north-western area of the mantapam. Two huge bells of the temple are located in the south-western portion of the mantapam. 
An inscription to be found on the northern wall (outer side) of the record room in the first prakaram of Tirumalai temple mentions about the construction of the Tiruma- mani mantapam by one Mallanna residing at Chandragiri. The inscription runs as follows:-1 
"Hail: On Wednesday, the day of Sravanam (star), being the 12th lunar day of the bright fortnight of the Simha month in the Hemulambi (Hevilambi) year, corresponding to the auspicious Saka year 1339, Mallanna alias Sri Madhava- dasar residing in Chandragiri (dedicated to Sri Venkatesa) the Tirumamani-mantapam (front portico), comprising the TIRUMUTTINADANDAL (beautiful flooring), KALDARAM (stone- foundation), the decorative work extending from the KURADU (basement) up to the STHUPI (roof) and the MEYAKKAL 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. I, Early Inscriptions, (1931) 
pp. 186-187. 
THE TEMPLE AND ITS SCULPTURES 
75 
(sloping terrace) over this, as being his construction (TIRUPPANI)". 
The date of the inscription has been worked out as the 25th August, 1417 A.D. 
This mantapam has 16 pillars. The pillars on the outer edge of the mantapam are of the complex type with the pillars resting on lions. All the pillars have very lovely bas-reliefs carved on them. A unique bas-relief on one of the pillars is the figure of Vishnu with four arms seated on an elephant. This is perhaps the only Vishnu murthi shown as seated on a Gajavahanam. The murthi has four arms; the upper two hold the chakra and the sankha. The lower right hand is in the abhaya hasta pose while the left hand rests on his thigh. The figure is seated in the sukhasana pose on the elephant. The left leg is folded at the knee while the right leg is dangling down rather gracefully. Another lovely bas-relief is that of Sitadevi seated on a platform giving her ring to Hanuman to be delivered to Sri Rama. Another impressive bas-relief is that of Prasanna Varaha Murthi, i.e. Vishnu in Varaha Avatar with his consort Lakshmi. This figure has four arms; the upper two hold the chakra and sankha while the lower right hand is in the abhaya hasta pose. The lower left hand is on the thigh of Lakshmi. A particularly im- pressive bas-relief about 27" high is that of Ugra Nara- simhamurthi emerging out of a pillar. This murthi has four arms; the upper right and left arms hold the chakra and sankha while He uses his lower right and left hands to emerge out of the pillar. Another peculiar bas-relief shows a couple; the man is in a bent position while his consort is playfully pulling him from behind. There is another impressive bas- relief of Sri Rama sitting on a throne. One of his hands is in the abhaya hasta pose. Lakshmana is standing by his side holding an arrow in his right hand and his bow in his 
76 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
left hand. Anjaneya is standing on the other side. His left hand is on his left knee and his right hand near his mouth. He appears to be giving some confidential news to his Lord. His tail is directed towards the sky. Other figures in the mantapam include the Kali Purusha on a flying horse, a warrior with a long sword and shield, Tara requesting Vali not to go to war with Rama, Dhanurdhari Sri Rama, Gopala Krishna, Srinivasa, etc. 
The Suprabhatam (the hymns waking up the Lord) is sung for the Lord in the Tirumamani mantapam. The Koluvu Srinivasa also holds his durbar in this mantapam. The mantapam is used for housing the processional deity on several special occasions. 
The Garuda Shrine:-Garuda is the vahanam or vehicle of Lord Vishnu. The shrine for Garuda was cons- tructed in the temple rather crudely after the construction of the Tirumamani mantapam in the year 1417 A.D. The earliest mention of Garuda in the Tirumalai Devasthanam inscriptions1 is in the year 1446 A.D. In the inscription bear- ing No. 17 G.T. it is seen the offerings given are only for the Garuda figure painted on the flag to be raised during the seven festivals "being the Tirukkodi Tirunal celebrated at Tirumala for Malaikiniyaninraperumal counted from the Adi festival to the Chittirai festival." The earliest inscription mentioning about the Garudalwar residing in his own shrine is in the year 1512 A.D. An inscription on the west wall of the second prakaram of the Tirumalai temple mentions of one Sriman Mahanayakacharya (Chief Commander) Periya Obula Nayakkar Rama Nayakkar propitiating the Garudalwar abiding in the shrine of Tiruvenkatamudayan with offerings of Tirupponakam such as chandanam, arecanuts and betel- 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. I, Early Inscriptions, (1931) 
pp. 219-221. 
THE TEMPLE AND ITS SCULPTURES 
77 
nuts, ghee for lighting lamps, and one atirasapadi. This inscription has been dated 14th July, 1512 A.D. We can therefore, safely infer that the Garuda shrine came into being about the period mentioned above. Inscriptions up to the end of the 15th century only mention about the propiti- ation of the Garuda image on the Garuda flag to be flown during the Brahmotsavam period and not of Garuda in the Archa form. It is therefore probable that the Garuda image as well as the Garuda shrine came into existence during the period between 1500-1512 A.D. 
The Garuda image in the Garuda shrine is about 5' high with hands in the anjali hasta pose. The wings are spread apart as if he is ready to fly away. Huge rings adorn his ears. He has several ornaments on his body. There is a small vimanam on his shrine. 
Bangaru Vakili:-At the western end of the Tiruma- mani mantapam is the Bangaru Vakili or the Door of Gold. We find two images of Jaya and Vijaya on both sides of this door. These are dwarapalakas or sentinels of the tem- ple. The images are made of copper. They are very beauti- ful. The images have four arms; the upper hands hold the chakra and sankha while one of the lower hands bears the Gada or mace. The other hand is in the suchi hasta pose, the pose in which we are warned to be clean in body and mind while entering the sanctum sanctorum. 
The Bangaru Vakili is unique in that it exhibits the various forms of Vishnu. According to Vaishnavite thought and teachings, Lord Vishnu manifests himself in various forms. These forms are the param, vyuham, vibhavam, antaryamin and archa forms. A brief description of these forms is given below.1 Para form is the type of the Sup- 
1. A hand book of South Indian Images by T.N. Srinivasan 
(1954) pp. 121-122. 
78 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
reme Deity as existing in the higher world beyond the ex- perience of human beings. This is referred to as Nitya Vibhuti and God is conceived to manifest Himself as des- cribed in the Vaikunta gadya of Sri Ramanuja-where he is known as Paravasudeva or Paramatman. 
Vyuham is the manifestation of the Paramatman in the apartment of his various functions of creation, sustenance and dissolution. They are in particular named as Vasudeva, Sankarshana, Pradhyumna and Aniruddha respectively. These forms of Vishnu are also inaccessible to the ordinary man. 
Vibhava type of Bhagawan is the accessible form to most blessed of the Lord's creations. They are the mani- festations of the Lord, through the several avataras and amsas like the Dasavataras of Vishnu. 
Antaryamin is the type of God as He exists in atomic form in the hearts of men. Though invisible He manifests Himself to the devotee by proper concentration and control of senses. By fervent prayers, His existence within one's own self can be easily realised and obeisance is made to Him by nivedana of food before taking it by Parishechanam. 
The more popular form of Supreme God is the Archa aspect, when His manifestation is easily tangible and is well felt by man. Sri Pillai Lokacharya says in his Arthapan- chaka: "The Archa form consists in the images of Bhaga- wan which accommodate themselves to the various tastes of his creatures, having no fixed form but that which the wor- shipper may choose and describe to call him by; all knowing but seeming as if not knowing; all powerful but seeming as if powerless; all sufficient but seeming as if needy, thus seeming to exchange places, the worshipped with the worshipper and choosing to be ocularly manifest to him in temples and homes, in short in all places and at all times desired." 
It is also significant that the Suprabhatam or daily 
THE TEMPLE AND ITS SCULPTURES 
79 
ceremony in which hymns are chanted to wake up the Lord, are sung before the Bangaru Vakili, which has a panel of all the forms of Vishnu, and not before the Archa form obtaining in the Garbha Griham. 
The Snapana Mantapam or Tiruvilankoyil:-Crossing the Bangaru Vakili, we enter a semi-lighted room which is the Snapana Mantapam or the Tiruvilankoyil. As already mentioned in Chapter II, Bhoga Srinivasa murthi was con- secrated in this mantapam in the year 966 A.D. We may therefore, presume that this mantapam existed in the early years of the 10th century A.D. itself. Sri T. K. T. Veera Raghavacharya is of the view that the pillars in the room are not original pillars and that the mantapam must have been renovated and alterations made. He is of the view that the original pillars were circular in origin while the pillars now in the mantapam are square in shape. These pillars them- selves bear a few good bas-reliefs. The bas-reliefs include the Garuda, bearded figures playing on drums, Bala Krishna in the Kaliya Mardana attitude, Yoga Narasimhaswamy in the yoga pose, a graceful woman dressed only up to the waist chastising her son under a tree, monkeys playfully fighting with each other, Kali Purusha riding a horse, etc. A parti- cularly impressive bas-relief is that of Maha Vishnu in the sitting pose. He has four arms. The upper arms hold the chakra and the sankha. The serpent Sesha is also portrayed. The Lord's consorts are seated in the sukhasana pose on his right and left. 
Ramar Medai:-Crossing the Tiruvilankoyil we enter the Ramar Medai. In the olden days the Ramar Medai and the incomplete first circumambulatory path now existing around the main shrine formed the Mukkoti Pradakshinam of the temple. This circumambulatory path however was closed and the Ramar Medai has been made into a closed 
80 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
room. Sri T.K.T. Veera Raghavacharya is of the view that the Ramar Medai was formed sometime during the period between 1262 and 1265 A.D. As a result of this, the Mukkoti Pradakshinam or the circumambulatory path around the Garbha Griham is open only on three sides. The Ramar Medai has two small platforms on which figures of Angada, Hanuman, etc. are exhibited. It has also a figure of a paricharika holding a light. This figure which is of bronze is about 2 feet high, 
Mukkoti Pradakshinam:-Around the original central shrine comprising of the Garbha Griham with its Mukha Mantapam called Sayana Mantapam, is the first circum- ambulatory path called the Mukkoti Pradakshinam. This Pradakshinam is opened in the temple only one day in a year i.e. the Vaikunta Ekadasi day. The Pradakshinam is open only on the northern, southern and western portions. The northern portion of the Pradakshinam is wider than the west- ern and southern sides. There is a small temple for Vishva- ksena also called the Senai Mudaliar on the northern side of the Mukkoti Pradakshinam. This murthi has four arms; the upper two hold chakra and sankha. The lower right hand is in the abhaya hasta pose while the lower left hand is rest- ing on his left leg just below the knee. He is shown seated in the sukhasana pose with the right leg dangling freely. Vishvaksena is recognised as the controller of the temple finances. This image is mentioned in one of the inscrip- tions1 on the south wall of the second prakaram in Tirumalai temple. This inscription states that the Senai Mudaliar at the shrine of Udaiyavar is to receive one appappadi at the time of reciting the iyal on a certain day and seven appappa- di a piece on the seven days during the adhyayanotsavam in 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. II, Inscription of Saluva 
Narasimha's time, pp. 192-198.THE TEMPLE AND ITS SCULPTURES 
81 
Tirumalai. The inscription is dated 27th June, 1491 A.D. The northern side of the Mukkoti Pradakshinam has also a small cement tank, into which flow the abhishekam waters of the Lord of Tirumalai from the Garbha Griham. The abhi- shekham waters are removed from the cement tank by hand using pots after the abhishekam is over. The walls of the Mukkoti Pradakshinam on the northern side are sculptured and bear stone columns of circular shape. There is an empty alcove on the northern side without any murthi installed in it. The stone alcoves in the Mukkoti Pradakshinam were perhaps built for the installation of the several murthis according to Vaikhanasa Agama; their installation was perhaps prevented by the followers of Sri Ramanuja who had a greater regard for the pancharatra form of worship of Lord Vishnu. The walls adjoining the Garbha Griham also show some Purnakumbha sculptures. Some of the circular stone columns are shown as emerging out of Purnakumbhas (vessels or pots that are full to the brim). 
The southern side of the Mukkoti Pradakshinam ís similar to that of the northern portion though very narrow in width. On the western side of the Mukkoti Pradakshinam are several circular pillars. The height of these pillars will be not less than 15' high. 
The Sayana Mantapam:-The Ramar Medai leads into the Sayana mantapam which is a room 18' 6" square. This mantapam is devoid of any noteworthy sculptures or structures. The Lord of Tirumalai is put to sleep in this mantapam during the Ekanta Seva at night as already mentioned. 
The Sanctum or the Garba Griham:-Behind the Sayana mantapam is the Garbha Griham or the Sanctum Sanctorum. The stone step between the Garbha Griham and the Sayana mantapam is called the Kulasekharappadi in honour of 
82 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
Kulasekhara Alwar. Devotees are not allowed to step on this or enter the Garbha Griham of the Lord of Tirumalai. 
The Garbha Griham is almost a square-shaped structure (12" square). The walls of Garbha Griham as well as the walls of Sayana mantapam, otherwise called the Mukha mantapam, are really double structures with two separate sets of walls enclosing some air space between them. This was perhaps necessitated by the construction of the additional structures comprising of the Mukkoti Pradakshinam built later. It is interesting to note that the Garbha Griham was called in the olden days as Koyil Alwar. The walls of the Garbha Griham as they exist at present are made up of cut- stone, and can be dated to belong to the 8th or 9th century A.D. at the earliest. 
The temple type consisting of a Garbha Griham with a Mukha mantapam with a Pradakshi- napatha got established in South India about the 8th century A.D. In view of this we cannot say with any degree of certainty that the present temple structure belongs to a period ealier than the 8th century A.D. This hypothesis does not in any way conflict with the tradition as well as the legend that the Lord's idol has been in existence at Tirumalai for ages. Earlier temples must have existed around the idol in the earlier days giving place in the 8th or 9th century A.D. to the cutstone structure existing at present. 
It is interesting to note that renovations of temples take place in all temples and Tirumalai temple is no exception in this regard. Thus for instance the following inscription1 bearing No. 17 T. T. found on the northern wall of the first prakaram of the Tirumalai temple shows that renovation of the shrine was done during the 40th year of the reign of Sri Veera Narasimha Yadavaraya. "Hail, Prosperity! On the 20th day in the month of Arpasi in the 40th year of the reign 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. I, Early Inscriptions, p. 120. 
THE TEMPLE AND ITS SCULPTURES 
83 
of Nayanar Vira-Narasingadeva Yadavarayar, on the receipt of the order of Nayanar by the Sthanattar (to the effect) that, at the time of the commencement by Tiruppullanidasar, one of the Desantaris, of the renovation of the shrine of Koyilalvar, the old inscriptions engraved on the central shrine built in the past shall be re-engraved at the north corner on the outer side of the first Prakaram, and the Stha- nattar having, in pursuance of the order, directed their re-engraving, this is the document so re-engraved on Friday combined with Uttiradam, being the 22nd day of the Chittirai month in the same year of reign, to wit." The inscription shows the date of the king's order permitting repairs as well as the date of completion of repairs. It would therefore not be strange to presume that the existing Garbha Griham was preceded in the olden times by structures which did not last long, or which were renovated or replaced sub- sequently. Support for such a hypothesis is available in traditional accounts. 
It only needs to be mentioned that the Garbha Griham houses only one Mula murthi and the temple in Tirumalai is unique in that it is the only Eka-murthi temple for Vishnu in India. 
CHAPTER V 
THE VENGADAM HILL, AND THE TEMPLE 
THEREON 
The Vengadam Hill according to the Puranas is the sporting hill of Lord Vishnu and was brought to earth from Vaikuntam by Garuda, the vehicle of Vishnu. The Puranic concept of Venkatachalam or Seshachalam is that it is a peak called Ananda-one of the peaks of Meruparvata- and that it is coiled by Adi Sesha. The connected legend is given in the Brahma Purana and the Bhavishyottara Purana. According to the Bhavishyottara Purana, once while Lord Sriman Narayana was in Vaikuntam, Sesha as Dwara- palaka prevented Vayu, the God of Winds, from entering Vaikuntam. Vayu and Sesha argued the matter, until the Lord intervened in the matter. Sesha then boasted that he was strong and that Vayu was not equal to him in strength. The Lord then said to him "Let there be a contest and I shall judge; Coil thyself on the peak Ananda which is an off-shoot of Meru; cling to the peak with all thy strength. Vayu shall then try to dislodge you from the hill." Vayu then tried to dislodge 'Sesha' concentrating all his power in his breath. Sesha then raised one of his heads for a moment, when Vayu blew off the peak along with Sesha. Meru then prayed to Vayu to spare his son, Ananda. Vayu therefore carefully placed the hill on the banks of the River Swarnamukhi. This is how Venkatachalam got the name Seshachalam; it is 
sacred to Vishnu. 
The Varaha Purana mentions that Vishnu in the Boar form and Srinivasa manifested themselves on the banks of the holy Pushkarini in Divya Vimanams on Venkatachalam, Kridadri brought from Vaikuntam to earth. The 
the 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 85 
Puranas also tell us that the Lord took his present archa form at the end of Dwaparayuga in his infinite grace and love towards the weak and sinning people of Kaliyuga on the request of Brahma and others. The celestials including Brahma are said to worship the Lord at Tirumalai as Nitya- suris, invisible to mortal eyes. In fact, when the temple doors are closed at night at Tirumalai all the articles for worship, including the gold and silver vessels with spiced water are left open in the sanctum for worship by celestials. The next morning the water in the vessels thus left is distri- buted as holy water to the devotees of the Lord. The Bhavishya Purana also mentions how the Lord's Svayam- vyakta idol was discovered by King Tondaiman in an ant- hill, under a tamarind tree on the banks of the Swami Push- karni. This Purana also gives the legend connected with the construction of the first temple of the Lord in Kaliyuga. Once King Tondaiman who came to worship the Lord of Tirumalai was commanded by him as follows:-"I have become a Grihasta or a householder. It is not proper that I should be houseless. Construct a temple for me. The credit for this shall be thine". Tondaiman then took an oath immediately that he would obey the Lord's com- mand. Lord Srinivasa and his consort Padmavati then selected the site for the temple on the southern bank of the Swami Pushkarini on Seshachalam. The Lord wished that his temple should have two gopurams, a Dhvajastambham, three prakarams, seven doors, the Asthana Mantapam, Yaga mantapam, a Gosala or a shed for cattle, houses for storing grain, flowers, oil, ghee and houses for dining, decoration, and ornaments. The temple was to be a struc- ture of stone and was to be ornamented with copper and gold. The King then constructed a temple for the Lord as directed. It was gem-studded, had Chathur-murties (four 
86 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
images) on it and was a splendid looking Vimanam. And the Lord then gladly accepted the Ananda Nilayam Vimanam as his residence. 
Another interesting puranic concept is that the Tiru- pati hills along with the hills of Ahobilam and the range of hills at Srisailam form the body of Adisesha. It is a geographically accepted fact that all these hills give the appearance of a cobra with its hood raised, basking in the open Sun. The seven hills of Tirupati are supposed to re- present the seven hoods of Sesha, and the Lord as Kaliya- mardana Krishna is presumed to dance on the Adisesha representing the divine rhythm in the limitless Cosmos. 
Venkatachalam is also mentioned in early classical Tamil literature. It is mentioned as 'Vengadam' hill in the ancient Tamil Grammar Tolkappiyam. The deity is how- ever not mentioned either in Tolkappiyam or by the Sangam Poet Mamulanar, (2nd Century A.D.) who also describes the 'Vengadam' Hill. The body of literature called Sangam literature which mentions about Venkata- chalam comprises of poems current in Tamilnad in the early ages. All this literature has been ascribed to a period earlier than 8th century A.D. 
A.D. Some of the poems coming under this literature throw some light on Venkata- chalam and its history. Poems from a work called the Ahananuru also refer to Tirupati as Vengadam, and mention of a 'Vaduku' Chief 'Pulli' as the ruler of 'Vengadam'. Pulli has been considered to be a Telugu Chief of Rayala- seema in Andhra Pradesh, ruling the Venkatachalam area in those days. Vaduku' appears to be the Tamil name for Telugu. Vengadam was in those days considered the northern border of Tamilnad, and the early works of Sangam litera- ture show that Vengadam was the place where the language of the Tamils changed from Tamil to 'Vaduku'. Another 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 87 
ruler Tirayyan, with his capital at Pavattiri, recognised to be the existing village of Reddipalayam, in the Gudur taluk of Nellore District in Andhra Pradesh is also mentioned in these works. It would appear that Venkatachalam area was then thickly forested, and elephants were found in plenty in the zone. The Chief 'Pulli' was recognised as one liberal in his gifts and a brave warrior. He was obviously the prince of hunters, hunting being the main occupation of the people in the forests around 'Vengadam'. In Mamulanar's poems Tirupati is also referred to as 'Pullikunram or the hill of the Chieftain Pulli. Mamulanar also mentions that Vengadam was prosperous because of the festivals on the hill. We could perhaps draw the in- ference that festivals on the hill were connected with the temple of Tirumalai. It may be remembered in this con- nection that according to the Puranas, Chakravarti Tondai- man after discovering the idol constructed a temple for the Lord and instituted festivals at Tirumalai. One of the early Alwars, Tirumalisai Alwar, also refers to the festival of 'Onavilavu' at Tirumalai; Onavilavu is obviously the same as the annual Brahmotsavam festival of Lord Srinivasa. 
The Tamil classic Silappadhikaram which is a work by a Jain (or a Buddhist?) also mentions and describes the Lord of Tirumalai standing on the hill of Tirupati as follows:1 "High on Vengadam's towering crest, with flowing 
streams in flood, 
Betwixt the effulgent glory, of shining Sun and Moon, Like unto a blue cloud in lightning dress 
In all the brilliance of rainbow light, 
The Red-eyed great One, majestic stands 
In dress of flowery brilliance with garland bright, 
1. As quoted from Dr. S. Krishnaswamy Aiyangar's History of 
Tirupati, Vol. I. 
88 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
One lotus hand with fearsome disc adorned, and 
milk-white conch (the other held)". 
The author of this work, one Ilango-adigal, is presumed to belong to the 18th century A.D. The work indicates that there was a Vishnu image with discus and conch on 'Vengadam' hill. 
The Alwars also in their songs have made detailed re- ferences to Tirumalai and the Lord thereon. Among the twelve Alwars or Vaishnava saints the early Alwars are Poyagi Alwar, Bhutam Alwar, Pey Alwar and Tirumalisai Alwar. According to tradition, the first three Alwars ob- tained enlightenment of God in the village of Tirrukkovilur.1 It appears that all the three Alwars were thrown together on a stormy night and that Poygai Alwar made himself com- fortable on the narrow pial of a small house in the village. Bhutam Alwar then knocked at the door and requested for admission. Poygai Alwar admitted him in spite of the fact that there was only space for one person to lie down on the pial and both of them had to sit up all the night on the pial. Late in the night, Pey Alwar also knocked on the door and the first two accommodated him though all of them had to remain standing on the pial for lack of space. Lord Vishnu and Lakshmi are then said to have knocked on the door. They were also admitted! Vishnu then slowly squeezed out his three devotees. While they were being thrown out, it dawned on them that Lord Vishnu was with them and testing them. The three Alwars then spontaneously broke into songs of praise of the Lord. The first Poygai made the whole universe the lamp vessel, the ocean the ghee for feed- ing the lamp, the Sun Himself the burning wick, and, light- ing such a lamp, he placed at the lotus feet of the One with the blazing disc, his garland of verses in order that the great 1. From Nityanusandhanam (Telugu) Vavilla Ramaswami Sas- 
trulu & Sons, Madras (1953). 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 89 
ocean of evil besetting him may leave him. The second in his own way made his own loving devotion (anbu) the lamp-vessel, his ardour (arvam) for service the ghee for feeding the lamp, and his mind melting with goodness, the lamp wick. He lighted the lamp of true knowledge (gnana) and dedicated it to God Narayana, as one capable of in- corporating his divine knowledge in Tamil verse. The third on the contrary broke out 'Lo, I see the Goddess Sri. I see the golden body, I see the colour of the rising Sun. I see the glorious disc. I see the dextral conch. I see all this in Him of the colour of the ocean, dear to me'.1 
The compositions of the first Poygai Alwar make several references to Tirumalai and the Lord of Tirumalai. A verse quoted from Dr. Krishnaswamy Aiyangar's History of Tirupati reads as follows:- 
"He rides the bull and bird 
He burnt the castle (the three castles in the air) And broke open the heart (tore up Hiranya Kasipu's) Chest with his claws as Narasimha. 
He is smeared over with ash (Vibhuti). 
He is of the saphire blue colour. 
Part of His body is a Lady (Parvati), 
And in one part is the Lady born of the lotus, 
Sri or Lakshmi. His coiffure, the long 
Matted locks. His head (is) covered by a tall crown; He wears the Ganga (Ganges) on His head (Siva), And on His lengthening foot (Vishnu Trivikrama)". Another of his verses has already been quoted in Chapter II. 
This Alwar appears to have regarded the Lord of Tirumalai as a combination of the Vishnu and Siva. 
The second, Bhutam Alwar, author of the work 'Irandan 
1. As quoted from Dr. S. Krishnaswamy Aiyangar's History of 
Tirupati, Vol. I. 
90 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
Thiruvandadi', also a devotee of Vishnu, regards the Lord of Tirumalai in one verse as the One who destroyed Ravana. Like Poygai Alwar he also visualised the Supreme Deity as a combination of the two forms Siva and Vishnu or as Hari-Hara. 
The third in the list of early Alwars is Pey Alwar, author of 'Mundran Thiruvandadi', who also recognises the twin aspects of Hari and Hara of Lord Vishnu. Two of his verses clearly mention (quoted in Chapter II of the Book) that the Lord of Tirumalai has combined into One-the forms of Siva and Vishnu. 
The next Alwar who engages our attention is Tiruma- lisai Alwar, the author of 'Naalaan Thiruvandadi'. Accord- ing to tradition he belonged to the village Thirumalisai near Madras. He was probably a 'Chandala' by caste. He was a great devotee of Lord Vishnu and the first of the Alwars who shows intolerance of the worship of other deities such as Siva, firm in the view that Lord Narayana is the one and only Deity that matters in the Universe. 
The next Alwar who merits our consideration is Nammalvar, the greatest of Alwars of South India. malvar was the son of Sudra parents and was born in the divya kshetra 'Sri Kuru Kuru' on the banks of the river Tamra Parni. He is also considered to be the Guru to the He is the Alwar Madhura Kavi according to tradition. author of the famous works Thiruviruttam, Tiruvasiriyam, Peria Thiruvandadi and Thiruvaymozi. The four works are renderings of the four Vedas, Rig Veda, Yajur Veda, Atharvana Veda and Sama Veda. His compositions are the most important in the Prabandham collection of verses of the Alwars called the 'Nalayira Prabandham'. 
He is also called Satakopacharya as he is credited with vanquishing 'Sata Vayu'-the Vayu that causes ignoranceTHE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 91 
in man. He is said to have been born in the year 798 A.D. and lived for about 35 years. He is considered to be an in- carnation of Vishnu, born specially to compose the 'Dravida Veda' in Tamil. Actually his Tiruvaymozhi is considered to be equal in merit, if not more sacred and merit-giving, with the Bhagavadgita. In his works, he shines as the greatest exponent of Bhakti, love and self-surrender to God. His love for the Lord is that of the love-lorn maiden pining away for her lover. In his works, he is at times a 'Sakhi' or a girl friend to the Lord, or a maiden pining for the love of the husband or lover. At other times he is the Mother of a maiden pining to join her Lord. 
The gist of a few of his verses relating to Lord of Tirumalai from Tiruvaymozhi are given below.1 
"The Valar Voli Mayan, or the Sarveswara with his divyamanohara mangala murthi and divya gunas has mani- fested himself with pleasure on Tirumaalirumsolai, surround- ed by Divya Udyanavanas. Worship Him while thou art young and before old age overtakes thee". 
"The butter is preserved in pots hung high to the roof but Krishna delights in stealing it and consuming it avidly with his friends. Let us then follow the path to Tirumaali- rumsolai, which is the 'koli' or temple for this Krishna." 
"The Lord who destroyed Puthana has his 'koil' in Tirumaalirumsolai. Let us not have thoughts that lead us to sin, but only think that his Lord should be worshipped and conquer Samsara." 
"The one who says 'Vengadattu Uraivarkku Namo Venatam Athu' or the one who says 'I bow to the Nira- vadhika Prabhava Sampanna Murthi Sriyahpathi who has 
1. From Nityanusandhanam a Vaishnavite work in Telugu about the Alwars. Vavilla Ramaswami Sastrulu and Sons, Madras, 1953. 
92 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
manifested Himself on Tirumalai' is released from all sins. All his sins get burnt to ashes." 
Nammalvar is also of the view that the Lord of Tiru- malai has the Rudra, Brahma and Lakshmi aspects of Vishnu in Himself and that these deities form a part of the Lord and have no independent existence of their own. 
The other Alwars are Madhura Kavi, Perialwar, Perial- war's foster daughter Goda Devi, Kulasekhara Alwar, Thondaradippodi Alwar, Tiruppanalvar and Tirumangai 
author of the Alwar, 
work 
Alwar. Madhurakavi "Kanninun Siruttambu', said to have been born in 797 A.D. was the disciple of Nammalvar. Nammalvar is said to have handed over his famous works for preservation and pro- pagation to Madhurakavi Alwar. Perialvar was born in Srivilliputtur and is the author of the famous 'Pallandu- Pallandu' and 'Perialvar Tirumozhi'. Perialvar is also called Sri Bhattanatha, Vishnuchitta etc. During his time, the King who ruled Madura was the Pandya ruler, Vallabha Deva Raya. He convened a conference of all Vidvans and sages of his time to decide the 'Paratatva'. It is said that Perialvar attended the conference on the directions of the Lord and established that the Paratatva was 'Sriman Narayana'. It is then said that a Vidya sulka nidihi, the prize tied in the royal courthall fell down at the feet of Perialvar, proving that he alone was eligible for the treasure. Some of his verses show the emotions of a love-lorn maiden pining for the love of her Lord Krishna. Andal, also called Goda Devi, was the foster daughter of Perialvar. She is the heroine of the famous Telugu Prabandham 'Amuktamal- yada' composed by Sri Krishnadeva Raya, the illustrious Vijayanagar Emperor. Goda Devi, also called Andal after 
1. From Nityanusandhanam, (Telugu) Vavilla Ramswami Sas- 
trulu & Sons, Madras, 1953. 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 93 
her Union with the Lord, was in the habit of herself wearing the garlands made for the 'malakainkaryam' of the Lord, looking at herself in a mirror to ensure that the garlands were worthy enough to be decorated for the Lord and then utilising them for the worship of the Lord. On one day Perialvar noticed Goda wearing the Lord's garlands and chastised her for the sin committed by her. That night Lord Vishnu is said to have appeared to him and informed him that the garlands worn first by Goda were acceptable as well as dear to him! 
Goda Devi was a devotee of Lord Vishnu and desired to wed Vishnu and no other. On her request, Perialvar described the 'Divya Vaibhavam' of the 'Perumals' in the 108 Divya Tirupatis. It is said that she was thrilled when her father described to her the glory of "Tiruvengadamu- daiyan of Tirumaalirumsolai'. She is said to have become unconscious with delight when the glory of Lord Sri Ranganatha of Sri Rangam was described and decided to wed Him. The Lord then accepted her and made her his consort. She is the author of the celebrated work 'Tiruppavai' and 'Nacchiyar Tirumozhi'. She never visited Tirupati and her references to Tirupati follow more or less the conventional descriptions of Vishnu. Her stanzas in Tiruppavai have great emotional appeal and excellence and stress the aspect of love between the love-lorn damsel and her Lord Krishna. 
Sri Kulasekhara, the author of 'Perumal Tirumozhi' the next Alwar, was the ruler of the Chera country (Travancore-Cochin) and was a Kshatriya saint devoted to Lord Vishnu. The gold-plated door-step of the Garbha Griham in the Tirumalai temple bears his name and is called Kulasekharappadi. Dr. S. Krishnaswamy Aiyangar is of the view that he belonged to the 7th century. His love 
94 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
for Tirumalai was great and in one of his poems he wishes that he should be born as a water or fish or a bush or as menial in the temple or as any other thing on the Tirupati hill howsoever mean to have the privilege of serving the 
Lord. 
Sri Thondaradippodi, a Brahmin saint, our next Alwar was a devotee of Sriranganatha. He is the author of the works "Tirupallieluchi' and 'Tirumalai'. He is famous in the Telugu country as Vipranarayana. His mode of serv- ing God was by 'mala-kainkarayam' that is by making flower garlands and offering them to the Lord. There is no re- ference to Tirupati or to the Lord of Tirumalai in his com- positions. 
The next Alwar, Sri Tiruppanalvar, author of 'Amala- nadipiran' (601 A.D.) was also a devotee of Lord Sriranga- natha of Srirangam. Only ten of his verses find place in the Tamil Prabandham; and there is only a general men- tion of the greatness of the Tirumalai temple in his verses. 
The last Alwar, Sri Tirumangai, belonged to the Sudra caste and became a saint after leading a riotous life. It is said that he fell in love with a woman who stipulated that she would become his wife if he fed one thousand and eight Brahmins a day for one full year. This he attempted to do by committing dacoities on the high-way. Once Lord Vishnu himself came to test him. And while the dacoit was stripping off the Lord of his ornaments (the ornaments on the toe), he realised who his victim was, and turned into the Lord's devotee. He was a great traveller visiting shrines all over India such as Devaprayag, Badrinath, Ahobilam etc. His references to the Lord of Tirumalai are more or less along the conventional lines. He is the author of the works, 'Peria Tirumozhi', 'Thirukkuruntandakam', 'Thiruneduntan- 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 95 
dakam', 'Thiruvezikuthirukkai', 
'Periathirumadal'. 
'Siriathirumadal' 
and 
Several other saints of South India have sung praises of the Lord of Tirumalai. Among them Kshetrayya, Thyagayya, Purandhara Dasa and the great Tallapakam poet Annamacharya, deserve special mention. 
Kshetrayya's real name is not known. He was a resi- dent of Muvva, a village in Krishna District in Andhra Pradesh. He toured all the holy Kshetrams in South India and composed songs on them. Hence the name Kshetrayya. He is a devotee of Lord Gopala Krishna of Muvva. All his songs (in Telugu) identify the Lord-wherever He is, whe- ther in Kanchipuram, or Hemadri or Tiruvellore etc.—as Muvva Gopala Krishna. His songs are famous in South India as 'Muvva Gopala Padas' and are usually sung with abhinaya by danseuses. In his songs, Kshetrayya identifies himself with the various kinds of Nayikas pining for the Lord's embrace. The compositions have Sringara or Love as their theme. The song below is an outpouring by a Virahothkan- titha Nayika 
It is my passion that has let me down! Oh! Friend with the face like the Moon! Envious wenches have borne tales to Him And its' my passion that has let me down, Should I go? Should I send an emissary? Should I venture to inform his well-wishers You know his mind; you know my state. Oh! Dame! Entreat Him to forget 
And forgive and return unto Me. 
Oh! Friend! Muvva Gopala Sri Venkata Ramana Joins me in the sport of the Lord of Love! 
And the memories of Yesterday 
96 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
Turn my body into water With pain and anticipation 
The Lord takes his revenge, 
And I cannot stand this passion. 
Oh! Friend! Unite me with my Lord! 
Another 'Padam' starts with the lines 'Muddu Betti Poyinade'. 
Giving me a kiss, 
He disappeared Oh! Mohanangi 
He made a sign and 
Entreated that I should not 
Prevent Him, kissing me. 
A particularly lovely 'padam' of Kshetrayya is by a 'Balintha' (a woman who has given birth and is in the early post-natal period) who entreats her Lord not to press her for the sport of the Lord of Love. 
This is no time for thee 
Oh! Lord! I shall not leave thee; tarry yet a-while Dazed by the fullness of my bodily lustre, 
Thou desirest to possess me. 
And when I chastise thee, thou behavest like a child. Oh! Rasika! Do not touch me in the breast, 
Thy hands are now full of milk 
....Oh! Sri Ranga! Muvva Gopala! 
Rein in thy mind for two months more, And I shall be ever thine. 
The great Andhra saint Thyagayya (1767-1847) has also sung the praises of the Lord of Tirumalai. He was a great devotee of Sri Rama and had the good fortune of obtaining darshan of his Ishta Daivam. His kritis or compositions on his Ishta Daivam, Sri Rama, are too well known to require mention here. His compositions are all in Telugu and form 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 97 
the bedrock, foundation, superstructure and glory of Carnatic Music in India. Thyagayya visited Tirupati in the year 1839. In his songs he refers to the Lord of Tiru- malai, as 'Tirupateesa (The Lord of Tirupati), Srinivasa, Venkatesa (The Lord of Venkata Hill) Seshagiri Sadana (The One who has Seshachalam as his residence).' 
On his entering the temple to worship the Lord, he found that a curtain had been hung up before the Lord of Tirumalai preventing him from having darshan. He then sang his famous Kriti in the Gowlipanthu raga (Adi talam) starting with the Pallavi "Théré Theeyyaga Rada Loni, Tirupati Venkata Ramana, Matsaramanu"-"Why not remove the curtain, Oh! Tirupati Venkata Ramana! Why not remove the inner curtain of Envy (in Men)." It is said that the curtain string snapped and that the curtain dropped down instantaneously revealing the Lord's glory to Thya- gayya! Another famous Kriti he sang (in the Madhya- mavathi raga, Adi talam) on the Lord of Tirumalai starts with the Pallavi "Venkatesa Ninu Sevimpanu Padivela Kannulu Kavalenayya". It is this song that contains the famous 'Charana' in it, "Ye, Nomu Phalamo Nee Nama- mruta Panamu Anu Sopanamu Dorikenu." 
"Oh! Venkatesa! A thousand eyes are indispensable to 
regard Thee! 
To see Thy divya-rupa manifest to sages blessed and free Oh! Lotus-eyes One! A thousand eyes are needed. 
As the fruit of some bygone age's worship 
I have, I have, found the way 
To imbibe the nectar of Thy name 
Oh! Lord of Lakshmi! Giver of Joy! 
Thyagayya is said to have sung a third song on Lord

Sri Venketeswara starting with Pallavi "Tharama Nee Mahima Pogada". 'Is it possible (for me) to sing Thy praises?' He is the author of several other Vishnu Kirtans. One Kirtana in the Udaya Ravi Chandra raga starting with the Pallavi "Yentha Nerchina, Yentha Juchina, Yentha Va- ralyna Kantha Dasule" is famous, for its pithy message to men of the materialistic world. The gist of the kirtan is as follows: 
Whatever the learning, Whatever the wisdom, Whatever the greatness, In spite of all these 
Man is slave to Woman 
Until he is a slave 
To thoughts that lead 
To Srikantha, the Lord of Lakshmi. Man tells lies and desires 
For Woman; for fortune, Living and fame

Oh! Lord! Praised be by Thyagayya! 
Purandhara Dasa, the great Saint of Mysore, famous for his Krithis on 'Vittal' is also said to have visited Tiru- malai and sung the praises of the Lord. Tallapaka Anna- macharya is then said to have requested him to sing a few of his compositions and declared that Purandhara Dasa was an incarnation of Shri Panduranga Vittalanatha. Anna- macharya in his turn was requested by Purandhara Dasa to sing a few of his compositions. Purandhara Dasa is then said to have declared that Annamacharya was an incarnation of Lord Srinivasa! 
The Tallapaka poets of Tallapaka village in Cuddapah District who have composed several songs on the Lord of 
THE VENGADAM HILL AND THE TEMPLE THEREON 99 
Tirumalai then deserve consideration. All the songs com- posed by these poets have been engraved on copper plates and preserved in the Tirumalai temple in an 'arai or closet called the 'Tallapaka Arai'. Two bas-reliefs are to be seen on the stone walls of the 'Arai' in the Vimana-Pradakshinam of the temple. They show figures of Tallapaka Annama- charya, the greatest of the Tallapaka poets and his son Peda Tirumalacharya. 
Tallapaka Annamacharya was born in the year 1414 and lived to the ripe old age of 92 years and expired in the year 1503. He has to his credit thirty two thousand compo- sitions on the Lord. These are all in the Yoga, Vairagya and Sringara styles. One of the Tallapaka poets Chinnaya considered to be the father of the Bhajana or devotional song in South India has also composed several 'bhajana' 
songs. 
The songs of Tallapaka poets are to this day sung in the temple of Tirumalai, especially at the time of the Lord's Ekanatha Seva. A descendant of the Tallapaka poets is given the honour of singing them. 
A free translation of one of the Sringara compositions of Annamacharya is given below: 
The love of the spouse 
Unto her Lord should be like this 
Striving for thy happiness always. 
Oh! Lord! In sport you pulled her Payyada-Kongu1 
And the flowers from her hair showered on thee 
And the Lord of Love then showered his arrows on her 
And she dazzled and struck, embraced thee. 
And while you sported with her 
The dust of camphor (from her body) 
Clung to thee!

In dalliance with thy consort 
Thou perspirest, With drops of sweat Spouting out of thee like from a pump And thy astonished bride 
Impeaches thee softly and clings to you In a long long embrace. 
The Eka Murthi Temple:-In the previous Chapter, it has been mentioned that the temple of the Lord of Tirumalai is unique in that it is an Eka Murthi temple. In such a temple, the Vimanam is to be found on the Garbha Griha only and the Garbha Griham is square in shape. 
The Eka Murthi temple is one in which there is only one Mula-murthi in the sanctum-sanctorum.CHAPTER VI 
ANANDA NILAYA VIMANAM 
The holy gopuram or tower over the Garbha Griha of a temple is called the Vimana. The Vimana, the thirtham, the stalavriksham or sacred tree of a Kshetram, the Perumal or the Lord and the Thayar or the Lord's consort are usually considered the 'Musts' for every temple in South India. The shrine itself is complete when it has (1) the Garbha Griha or the sanctum-sanctorum, (2) the Bimbam or the Image in the shrine and (3) the Vimanam or tower on the top of the Garbha Griham. Sometimes the term 'Vimanam' is used as a synonym for the temple itself as in the Bhavishyottara 
Purana. 
The word Vimana comes from the root 'Ma' which is preceded by the sound 'V' and is supposed to measure and is considered to be a representation of the Cosmos. The Vimanam on the Lord's temple at Tirumalai is called the Anandanilaya Vimanam. 
"Ananda janakathvattamananda Nilayam Viduhu" 
Ananda stands for bliss, nilaya is the house and Anandanilaya is the Abode of Bliss. The Tirumalai temple is an abode of bliss. Therefore we may agree that the Vimana of the temple is aptly called Anandanilaya Vimanam. This Vimana is supposed to inspire the very best in mankind by its very sight and lead them to Ultimate Bliss. From another point of view, the ascent of the seven hills of Tiru- malai and the first vision of Anandanilaya Vimanam of the temple on the Ananda Hill represents the ascent of the Kundalini Shakti in the human body to the Sriman Narayana reclining on a Sahasra-dala-Padma and the achievement of Oneness with the Eternal One. 
The Vimanam on the temple of the Lord is a celestial 
102 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
Vimanam. The Varaha Puranam mentions that when the Lord manifested himself on the Swami Pushkarini, it was in a Divya Vimanam which arrived from Sri Vaikuntam. Lord Brahma on perceiving the Divya Vimanam praised it as 
इदं तु दिव्यं परमाद्भुतं शुभं विमानमिन्द्रादिनिषेव्यमाणम् । 
विभाति विष्णोरिव मंन्दिरं परं पश्याम सर्वे वयमद्भुतं गृहम् ॥ 
The Varaha Puranam also mentions that this Divya Vimanam of Vaikuntam will be invisible to mortal eyes in Kaliyuga and that men will construct a separate Vimanam for the Lord. 
The Bhavishyottara Puranam also mentions about the Divya Vimanam as follows. 
तत आनंदनिलये तोण्डमानृपनिर्मिते । 
विमानाग्रे श्रीनिवासो रराज भगवान् हरिः ॥ 
From this quotation it is clear that the first Vimanam1 for the Lord by man was constructed by Thondaiman Chakravarthi. The kind of the temple actually constructed by Thondaiman Chakravarthi as well as the details of the Vimanam constructed by him are not known to us, the only references to the temple and the Vimanam constructed by him being only legendary. The structures put up if any had only a short life. From a study of the architecture of the Garbha Griham it has already been mentioned that the Tirumalai temple cannot be dated earlier than the 8th century A.D. Perhaps the existing Vimanam at Tirumalai was first constructed round about the period indicated above. At any rate, this cannot be later than the year 1262 A.D. 
The first time the Vimanam was gilded was during the time of the Vijayanagar King Veera Narasingadeva. It is said that this king preformed the Thularohana ceremony of 
1. Used as a synonym for the temple including the Vimanami. 
ANANDA NILAYA VIMANAM 
103 
weighing himself in scales against gold and presented all the gold to the temple for gilding the Vimanam of the temple. The relevant inscription1 found on the door-jamb wall of the Padikkavali gopuram in Tirumalai temple reads as follows: "Hail, Prosperity! The prosperous king Vira-Nrisimha- deva, having conquered the enemies in war, extended his fame over the earth and wedded the Goddess of Prosperity with the emblems of a garland, an elephant, a white umbrella and other insignia (of royalty), and, having performed the Tularohana (ceremony), made Venkatagiri (Tirumala), through (the presentation, of) the weighing gold, equal to Suragiri (Mount Meru)." The King Veera Narasinga- devaraya of the Yadava Rayas was a powerful Raja of Thondamandalam comprising of the zamindari tracts of Kalahasti and Karvetinagara, together with portions of the Chingleput and Chittoor districts, the religious centres of Tiruvorriyur, Kalahasti and Tirupati being included within it.2 The presentation of gold by him was obviously for gilding the Vimanam of the temple and to make it shine as Mount Meru. His reign has been calculated to have taken place during the period between 1205 A.D. and 1262 A.D. The gilding of the Vimanam by Veera Narasingadeva Yada- varaya cannot be later than 1262 A.D. The Vimanam must therefore have existed earlier than this date. 
Another inscription found on the west face (right side of the first gopuram in Tirumalai temple) reads as follows: "Oh, King Sundara Pandya Deva;-the brilliance (of your body excels) the lustre issued by the golden vase (fixed by you over the temple)". 
This inscription refers to Jathavarma Sundara Pandya. 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. I, Early Inscriptions, (1931) 
page 123. 
2. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. I, Early Inscriptions (1931) 
Page 105. 
104 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
It shows us that Jathavarma Sundara Pandya fixed a 'Kanaka Kalasa' or a vase of gold on the temple Vimana. Jatha- varma Sundara Pandya ascended the throne in 1251 A.D. and ruled the Pandya kingdom until 1275 A.D. About the tenth year of his reign, he led his armies to Nellore. On his return journey to Kanchipuram he might have visited the temple and arranged for the fixation of the vase of gold on the temple Vimanam. The date of fixation of the Kalasam is not known, but it should have been during the period bet- ween 1251 and 1275 A.D. Perhaps the gilding of the Vima- nam by Veera Narasinga Deva as well as the fixation of the Kalasam took place round about the period 1262 A.D. 
The next gilding of the temple Vimanam was done by one Saluva Mangideva in the year 1359 A.D. The relevant inscription reads as follows':1 "Hail, Prosperity: On Satur- day, the 10th (lunar) day of the bright fortnight in Ashadha in the (cyclic) year Vikari, corresponding to the victorious Saka year 1281, the illustrious Mahamandalesvara Misara- ganda Mangideva Maharaja fixed a golden Sikhara (vase) over the Vimana (dome) of Tirumaladeva (Tiruvengada- natha). May prosperity abide". The inscription indicates that a golden sikhara, that is a vase, was fixed over the Vi- mana of the Tirumalanayaka temple. The Vimanam itself was also covered with gilded copper plates. This Saluva Mangideva was a General under Kumarakampana Vadayar. 
The next benefactor associated with the renovation of the Vimana is Amatyasekhara Mallanna, a Minister under Devaraya II. Mallanna was also called Sri Madhavadasar and was a minister under Devaraya II. He not only cons- tructed the Tirumamani mantapam in front of the central shrine, but also renovated Ananda Vimanam over the sanc-

tum as can be surmised from a few readable broken sentences in inscription No. 235 T.T. which reads as follows. "I.. being the disciple.... 2....Sri Madhavadasar....3.... Ananda-Vimana....4....executed....5.... Panam.... The broken sentences include the critical words Sri Madhava- dasar and Ananda-Vimana. We may not therefore be wrong in assuming that Sri Madhavadasar renovated the temple Vimanam. From the inscriptions of Tirumalai, it is seen that the dates of his earliest and latest inscriptions are 13-3-1409 and 2-10-1444 A.D. respectively. His construction of the Tirumamani mantapam in the temple was in 1417 A.D. We may not be wrong in assuming that the renovation of the Ananda Vimanam was also round about the year 1417 A.D. and at any rate not later than the year 1444 A.D. 
Sri Krishnadevaraya of Vijayanagar fame is the next in our list of benefactors who improved the Anandanilaya Vimana. The inscription2 reproduced below indicates that he got the Divya Vimanam of the Lord Venkateswara gilded in the year Bahudhanya corresponding to 9-9-1518 A.D. 
"Hail! Prosperity! Sriman Maharajadhiraja Rajapara- meswara Mururayana-ganda Ariyarayavibhata Ashtadikra- yamanobhayankara Bhashagutappuvarayana-ganda Purva- 
dakshina-paschima-samudradhisvara Yavanarajya-sthapana- charya Gajapati-Vibhata Sri Virapratapa Sri Vira Krishna- deva Maharaya- 
"Started from his capital Vijayanagara, on an eastern expedition, occupied the fort Udayagiri, captured Rauta- raya Mahapatra, in one single campaign took Addanki, Vinu- konda, Bellamkonda, Nagarjunikonda, Tangeda, Ketavaram and other forts situated on hills and plains, next marched

SRI VENKATESWARA 
to Kondavidu fortress, laid siege to it, erected square sheds round the fort, demolished the rampart walls, occupied the citadel, captured alive Virabhadraraya, son of Prataparudra Gajapati, Naraharideva, son of Kumara Hamvirapatra, Ra- churu Mallukhan, Uddandakhan, Janyala Kesavapatra, Pusa- pati Rachiraja, Srinatharaja Lakshmipatiraja, Paschimabala- chandra Mahapatra and other Patrasamantas and Manneyers (Zamindars), granted them their lives and proceeded to Dharanikota-Amaresvara performing Tulapurusha Maha- dana, returned to Vijayanagara, ruled the country; 
"And again launching upon an expedition against Kalinga- desa, proceeded to Bezawada, occupied the fortress of Kon- dapalli, captured alive Praharaja-Siraschandra-Mahapatra, Botajana Mahapatra, Bijilikhan and others who were ruling over the fort, granted them their lives, in one single attack took possession of Anantagiri, Undrakonda, Urlakonda, Aru- vapalli, Jallipalli, Kandikonda, Kappaluvayi, Nallamkonda, Kambammettu, Sankaragiri and other forts in the Telugu- rajya, reached Simhadri-potnuru, planted a pillar of victory and performed a Mahadanam there and then returned to Rajamahendravara, had Mahadanas performed by his queens Chinnadeviamman and Tirumaladeviamman and then went back to Vijayanagara and when ruling the country; 
"On Thursday, combine with the star Svati, being the 5th lunar day of the bright fortnight of the Kanya month in the cyclic year Bahudhanya current with the Saka year 1440, completed the gilding work of the Divya-Vimanam of Sri Venkatesa as his dharman (charity)". 
The gilding was obviously done by Krishnadevaraya after his triumphant march from Rajamundry to Vijaya- 
nagaram. 
The Vimanam was also gilded in the year 1630 A.D. by one Koti Kanyakadanam Thathacharya of Kanchi. 
ANANDA NILAYA VIMANAM 
107 
The gold kalasa over the Vimanam was again fixed by one Ramalakshmanadasa, one of the brother disciples of Sri Mahanth Prayagadasa in the year 1908 A.D. The relevant inscription reads as follows:1 "Salutation to Sri Venkatesa. Ramalakshmanadasa, one of the brother-disciples of Mahant Prayagadasa, the then Vicharanakarta of these Devasthanams arranged for the fixing of the kanaka-kalasa (golden vase) over the Vimanam of Venkateswara's central shrine on the 5th lunar day of the bright fortnight of the month of Asva- yuja in the year Kilaka, current with the Kaliyuga year 5010". 
The latest renovation and rebuilding of the Vimanam was done by the Tirupati-Tirumalai Devasthanam Committee a few years ago. The Committee got the Gopuram com- pletely rebuilt in the year 1958. The decision to repair the leaky Vimana was taken in the year 1952 and the work started on 16th June 1953 after the construction of a Balalayam transferring the thejas of the Mula-murthi to a bimbam in the Kalyana mantapam. The renovation was done at a cost of Rs. 18 lakhs using about 12,000 tolas of gold costing Rs. 12 lakhs. The casting of the copper plates required costed about Rs. 2.5 lakhs. 
The Anandanilaya Vimana2 is a three-storeyed structure with a square base of 27' 4" and a height of 37' 8" including the kalasa over the Garbha Griha. It has three storeys, the first, second and third measuring 10', 10' 9" and 16" 3". The first two tiers are rectangular in shape while the third is circular in shape. The Vimanam at present is completely gilded. Gilded copper sheets have been fixed to the original Vimanam and the space between the sheets and the Vimanam filled up with cement concrete. 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series Vol. VI, Part I, Inscriptions of 
Venkatapatiraya's time, pp. 225-226. 
2. Ananda Nilaya Vimanam-an article by the Architect V. M. 
Narasimham, T.T. Devasthanam's Bulletin, 27-8-1958. 
108 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
Only a few bas reliefs are seen on the first tier of the Anandanilaya Vimanam. There are about forty such figures on the second tier and these include figures such as Anjaneya, Garuda in the anjali hasta pose, seated Vishnu with four arms, Trivikrama, Lakshmi, Kodandapani Rama, Kaliyaphanimardana Krishna etc. The Vimana Venkates- wara is to be seen on this tier. This image is a small replica of the Lord's image in the sanctum. It is interesting in this connection to remember that Vyasa Raja or Vyasa thirtha, the famous Madhva Saint was in the habit of worshipping this Vimana Srinivasa and then only taking his food for the day. The pilgrims of the Madhva community to this day read the Puranas in the Vimana Pradakshina after worship- ping the Vimana Srinivasa. The third tier consists of about twenty bas-reliefs. It has the figure of a lotus or a Maha- padmam on it. The lovely standing lion figures on the Vimana are worth seeing among the 'bimbas' of the Vima- nam. The bas-reliefs of this tier include Vishnu murthi with four arms in the Sukhaasana pose, Garuda etc. The forms of Vishnu on the Vimana are those of the Param, Vyuham, Vibhavam, Antaryamin and Archa forms, according to one view. 
The Maha samprokshanam or the purificatory and bles- sing ceremony of the Divya Vimanam took place at Tiruma- lai in the last week of August, 1958. The Ananda Nilaya Vimanam has since then been gladdening the hearts of weary pilgrims who went their way up the seven hills of Tirumalai to worship the Lord. 
CHAPTER VII 
SRI VENKATESWARA SUPRABHATAM 
'Suprabhatam' is the Melukolupu or the waking up ceremony of the Lord of Tirumalai every morning. This ceremony is performed every day in the Tirumalai temple before dawn at about 4 A.M. The priests and the devotees who congregate for the 'Suprabhatam' assemble near the 'Bangaru Vakili' of the Golden Gate, in the sixteen-pillared Tirumamani mantapam and sing the praises of the Lord. These slokas awakening the Lord and at the same time in- voking his blessings were composed (according to tradition) by one Prativadi Bhayankara Annan, said to be a contempo- rary of the great Visisthadvaitic sage Sri Vedanta Desika.1 The composer of the Suprabhatam being considered a con- temporary of Sri Vedanta Desika, we may roughly take it that the Suprabhatam might have been composed in the later years of the fourteenth century. The singing of these slokas in the temple might have therefore commenced in the later years of the fourteenth century or perhaps even a little later. The Vedas were being chanted in the temple before the fifteenth century, as we know that Sri Virapratapa Deva- raya Maharaya ordered the congregational singing of the Vedas in Tirumalai in the year 1430 A.D., thus restarting a practice which had long gone into disuse. It is possible that the Suprabhatam formed a part of the congregational singing of the Holy books in the temple in the fifteenth century. 
The Suprabhatam is an impressive devotional poem 
1. Sri Vedanta Desika, a native of Kanchipuram, was born in the year 1268 and is said to have expired after living a full hundred years in the year 1368. 
110 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
comprising of twenty-nine slokas. Another stotram, the Sri Venkateswara stotram comprising of eleven Sanskrit slokas also sings the praises of Sri Venkateswara. This Suprabha- tam however is unique for its content of intense devotion to Vishnu. The first thirteen verses have a higher poetic and emotional value than the remaining sixteen verses. Some of the verses have a fanatical tinge in playing down Siva and other Gods, and give a pointer to the conflicts between Vaishnavism and Saivism in the fourteenth century in South India. 
Assuming that the singing of these hymns started in 1430 A.D. the year in which Sri Virapratapa Deva Raya Maharaya ordered Vedaparayanam in the temple, it will be seen that these hymns have been sung in the temple for about 542 years at least and have thus attained great value also. Hinduism has recognised among all the world's reli- gions, the oneness of ail Gods. Beautiful phrases like 'Jaga- deka Dayaika Sindho', 'Jagadeka Saranyamurthaye,' 'Samsara Sagara Samuttaranaikasetho' which are used by the author, indicate that he adored Vishnu as the One, and the Only God. 
The gist of the slokas of the Suprabhatam has been given below. Some of the verses lend themselves to slightly differ- ent interpretations. These aspects have not been comment- ed upon while translating the slokas. The simplest and most acceptable interpretation has only been given, keep- ing in view the need for brevity. 
१. 
Oh! 
कौसल्या सुप्रजा राम पूर्वा सन्ध्या प्रवर्तते । 
उत्तिष्ठ नरशार्दूल कर्त्तव्यं दैवमाह्निकम् ॥ 
Noble son of Kousalya! The twilight heraldeth the Dawn. Oh! Purushottama! Awake for the due perfor- mance of thy divine nityakarma.SRI VENKATESWARA SUPRABHATAM 
२. उत्तिष्ठोतिष्ठ गोविन्द उत्तिष्ठ गरुडध्वज । 
उत्तिष्ठ कमलाकान्त त्रैलोक्यं मङ्गलं कुरु ॥ 
111 
Awake Oh! Govinda! awake awake! Thou with the Garuda Pennant! awake! Thou consort of Kamala! Awake to bestow all Mangalams on the three worlds. 
३. मातस्तमस्तजगतां मधुकैटभारेः वक्षोविहारिणि मनोहरदिव्यरूपे । 
श्रीस्वामिनि श्रितजनप्रियदानशीले श्रीवेङ्कटेशदयिते तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ Mother of all the worlds that dwelleth on the vaksha of the Destroyer of the demons Madhu and Kaitabha! Oh! Manohara Divyamurthi! Oh! Mahalakshmi, thou Bestower of wishes on thy devotees seeking thy protection, Oh! Con- sort of Lord Venkateswara ! Suprabhatam to you (Awake!). 
तव सुप्रभातमरविन्दलोचने भवतु प्रसन्नमुखचन्द्रमण्डले । विधिशङ्करेन्द्रवनिताभिचिते वृषशैलनाथदयिते दयानिधे ॥ 
An auspicious day is dawning for thee! Thou, Beloved of the Lord of Vrishabhadri! Oh! Lotus eyed One with the moon-like face of beauty! Thou art extolled by the Consorts of Brahma, Siva and Indra! Thou treasure-house of Daya or Kindness! Awake. 
५. अत्र्यादिसप्तऋषयस्समुपास्य सन्ध्यां आकाशसिन्धुकमलानि मनोहराणि 
आदाय पादयुगमर्चयितुं प्रपन्नाः शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Peak! Atri and other sapta rishis after their morning sandhya, have gathered lotuses from Akasa Ganga and await thee, to decorate and worship thy twin feet! May thy auspicious day commence. 
६. पञ्चाननाब्जभवषण्मुखवासवाद्याः त्रैविक्रमादिचरितं विबुधाः स्तुवन्ति । 
भाषापतिः पठति वासरशुद्धिमारात् शेषाद्विशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Peak ! Maheswara, Brahma, Kumaraswami, Mahendra and other supernal beings chant thy hymns as Trivikrama. Brihaspathi is reading the al- manac for you nearby! Awake. 
112 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
७. ईषत्प्रफुल्लसरसीरुहनारिकेल पूगद्मादिसुमनोहरपालिकानाम् । 
आवाति मन्दमनिलस्सह दिव्यगन्धैः शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
A gentle breeze loaded with the fragrance of half opened lotuses, coconuts, palms and other scented plants is blowing for thee! Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Peak ! Awake. 
८. उन्मील्य नेत्रयुगमुत्तमपञ्चरस्थाः पात्रावशिष्टकदलीफलपायसानि । 
भुक्त्वा सलीलमथ केलिशुकाः पठन्ति शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ।। The fancy parakeets with dilated eyes kept in worthy cages partake again the bananas and payasam left in the feeding vessels and sing gaily for thee! Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Peak ! Suprabhatam to you. 
९. तन्त्रीप्रकर्षमधुरस्वनया विपञ्च्या गायत्यनन्तचरितं तव नारदोऽपि । 
भाषासमग्रमसकृत्करचाररम्यं शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
The Sage Narada dexterously manipulates his sweet music-giving Vipanchi-Veena while he sings eloquent praises to thee! Oh! Ananta! Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Peak ! Awake. 
१०. भृङ्गावली च मकरन्दरसानु विद्धझङ्कारगीतनिनदैस्सह सेवनाय । 
निर्यात्युपान्त सरसी कमलोदरेभ्यः शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ Imbibing well the nectar of flowers, swarms of bees are emerging out of lotuses in the lakes, with humming notes of music to worship thee! Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Peak! Suprabhatam to you. 
११. योषागणेन वरदनि विमथ्यमाने 
घोषालयेषु दधिमन्थनतीव्रघोषाः । 
रोषात्कल विदधते ककुभश्च कुम्भाः 
शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
Curds are being churned in the households of cowherds by women. The echoes of the churning sounds appear as though the pots of curd and the bearings of the Universe are having an argument with each other. Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Hill! Awake. 
SRI VENKATESWARA SUPRABHATAM 
113 
१२. पद्मशमित्रशतपत्रगतालिवर्गाः 
हर्तुं श्रियं कुवलयस्य निजाङ्गलक्ष्म्या । 
भेरीनिनादमिव बिभ्रति तीव्रनादम् 
शेषाद्रिशेखरविभो तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
The Sun is the friend of the hundred-petalled lotus. The bees emerging out of such lotuses with their bodily lusters are stealing (or endeavouring to steal) the glory of the dark-coloured lotuses (Kuvalayasya) by buzzing aloud. Oh! Lord of the Seshadri Hill! Suprabhatam to you. 
१३. श्रीमन्नभीष्टवरदाखिललोकबन्धो श्रीश्रीनिवास जगदेकदयैकसिन्धो । 
श्रीदेवतागृहभुजान्तरदिव्यमूर्ते श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
Oh! Lord of Lakshmi who bestoweth boons! Kinsman of all the worlds! Sri Srinivasa! The only One in the whole of the Universe who art the Ocean of Kindness! Oh! Divya- murthi who art the residence of Lakshmi! Oh! Venkata- chalapati! Awake ! 
१४. श्रीस्वामिपुष्करिणिकाऽऽप्लव निर्मलाङ्गाः 
श्रेयोऽथिनो हरविरिञ्चसनन्दनाद्याः । 
द्वारे वसन्ति वरवेत्रहतोत्तमाङ्गा' 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। 
Brahma, Maheswara, Sanandana and others after a purificatory bath in the Swami Puskharini await thee near thy door with staffs and with bent heads. Oh! Lord of Venkata Hill! Awake. 
1. I believe the words ‘Hatha' in 'Varavetra Hatottamanga' is out of place and the correct text is 'Varavetra Natottamanga'. The former phrase is usually translated as with Uttamangas or heads being beaten by Vara Vetras or quality canes wielded by the Vetrahastas or Dwarapalakas in the temple'. Such an interpre- tation is prima facie absurd. 'Varavetra Natottamanga' reads better in the context. Another possible interpretation for 'Vara- vetra Natottamanga' is that the Uttamapurusha deities are pre- sent without their weapons.

१५. श्रीशेषशैलगरुडाचलवेङ्कटाद्रि

Thy residence is for ever being called variously as Sri Seshasailam, Garudachalam, Venkatadri, Narayanadri, Vrishabhadri etc. Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati! Awake. 
१६. सेवापराश्शिवसुरेशकृशानुधर्म रक्षोऽम्बुनाथपवमानधनाधिनाथाः । 
बद्धाञ्जलिप्रविलसन्निजशीर्षदेशाः श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। Oh! Lord of Venkata Hill! Siva, Indra, Agni, Yama, Nairuthi, Varuna, Vayu and Kubera with anjali hasthas wait for thee to worship thee! Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati! Awake. 
१७. धाटीषु ते विहगराजमृगाधिराज 
नागाधिराजगज राजहयाधिराजाः । 
स्वस्वाधिकारमहिमाधिकमर्थयन्ते 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। 
The Lords among birds, animals, snakes, elephants and horses, Garuda, Simha, Adisesha, Iravata and Vucchaisrava respectively (await to) solicit thy favour during thy outings to gain in merit and importance. Oh! Sri Venkatachala- pati ! Awake. 
१८. सुर्येन्दुभौमबुधवाक्पतिकाव्यसौरि स्वर्भानु केतुदिविषत्परिषत्प्रधानाः। त्वद्दासदासचरमावधिदासदासाः श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। The prominent deities of the Devasabha, Surya, Chandra, Angaraka, Budha, Guru, Sukra, Sani, Rahu and Ketu, await thee (even) as servitors to thy lackeys of the last degree. Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati ! Awake. 
१९. 
त्वत्पादधूलिभरितस्फुरितोत्तमाङ्गाः

115 
Thy devotees that shine by wearing thy dust on their heads, desire not either Heaven or Moksha; they grieve that another ‘kalpa’ may deny them thy grace. Oh! Sri Venka- tachalapati! Awake. 
२०. त्वद्गोपुराग्रशिखराणि निरीक्षमाणाः 
स्वर्गापवर्गपदवीं परमां श्रयन्तः । 
मर्त्या मनुष्यभुवने मतिमाश्रयन्ते 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। 
Men who have been blessed with Mukti and others who are on their way to Heaven notice the Gopuram and shika- ram on thy temple and desire to be (reborn) on the Earth 
(to serve thee ). Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati! Awake. 
२१. श्रीभूमिनायक दयादिगुणामृताब्धे 
देवाधिदेव जगदेकशरण्यमूर्ते । 
श्रीमन्ननन्तगरुडादिभिरचितात्रे

Sri Venkatachalapati ! Thou art the Lord of Sri Devi and Bhudevi! Thou art verily the ocean of Kindness and other Gunas! Oh! Devadi Deva! Thou art the Only Refuge for the entire Universe ! Oh! Lord! Thou art the One whose feet are worshipped by Ananta, Garuda and others! Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati Awake. 
२२. श्रीपद्मनाभ पुरुषोत्तम वासुदेव 
वैकुण्ठ माधव जनार्दन चक्रपाणे । 
श्रीवत्सचिह्न शरणागतपारिजात 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
1. A ‘kalpa’ runs for about a few lakhs of years. According to tradition, the Lord of Tirumalai is the Deity for Kaliyuga, in the Sweta Varahakalpam. The position may change in the Kalpa that follows. Hence the grief and the distress of the devotees of the Lord of Tirumalai.
