SRI VENKATESWARA 
Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati ! Sri Padmanabha ! Puru- shottama! Vasudeva! Vaikunta! Madhava! Janardana ! Chakrapani ! Thou art the One with the Srivatsa mole on thy body! Thou art like the Parijatha boon-bestowing-tree to those that seek thy protection! Awake. 
२३. कन्दर्प दर्पहरसुन्दरदिव्यमूर्ते 
कान्ताकुचाम्बुरुहकुड्मललोलदृष्टे । 
कल्याणनिर्मलगुणाकरदिव्यकीर्ते 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
Oh! Divyamurti ! Thy handsome form is the cor- rective to Manmatha's vain-glory (that he is handsome!). Oh! Lord with thy gaze fixed on the lotus-bud-like breasts of thy consort! Thou art renowned for thy auspicious and blemishless qualities (of goodness) ! Oh! Sri Venkatachala- pati! Awake. 
२४. मीनाकृते कमठ कोल नृसिंह वर्णिन् 
स्वामिन् परश्वथतपोधन रामचंद्र । 
शेषांशराम यदुनन्दन कल्किरूप 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। 
Oh! Lord! Thou art (verily no other than) the Avatars of Matsya, Kurma, Varaha, Narasimha, Vamana, Parasu- rama, Sri Rama, Balarama, Sri Krishna and Kalki. Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati ! Awake. 
२५. एलालवङ्गघनसारसुगन्धतीर्थं 
दिव्यं वियत्सरिति हेमघटेषु पूर्णम् । 
धृत्वाऽद्य वैदिकशिखामणयः प्रहृष्टाः 
तिष्ठन्ति वेङ्कटपते तव सुप्रभातम् ।। 
Scholars well-versed in the Vedas, carrying on their heads receptacles of gold containing the fragrant waters of the Akasa Ganga well spiced with cardamoms, cloves and Pacchaikarpuram, are waiting for thee in joy (to worship thee!). Oh! Venkatachalapati! Awake. 
SRI VENKATESWARA SUPRABHATAM 
२६. भास्वानुदेति विकचानि सरोरुहाणि 
संपूरयन्ति निनदैः ककुभो विहङ्गाः । 
श्रीवैष्णवास्सततमथितमङ्गलास्ते 
धामाश्रयन्ति तव वेङ्कट सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
117 
Oh! Lord of Venkata Hill! The Sun is rising. The lotuses are opening out in full bloom. The birds are filling the air with birdsound. And the Srivaishnavas wishing for eternal auspiciousness wait for thee ! Awake. 
२७. ब्रह्मादयस्सुरवरास्समहर्षयस्ते 
सन्तस्सनन्दनमुखास्तव योगिवर्याः । 
धामान्तिके तव हि मङ्गलवस्तुहस्ताः 
श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
Brahma and other celestials, Satpurusha yogis such as Sanandana and other sages with auspicious articles of wor- ship in their hands await thee! Oh! Sri Venkatachalapati! Awake. 
२८. लक्ष्मीनिवास निरवद्यगुणैकसिन्धो संसारसागरसमुत्तरणैकसेतो । 
वेदान्तवेद्यनिजवैभव भक्तभोग्य श्रीवेङ्कटाचलपते तव सुप्रभातम् ॥ 
Oh! Abode of Lakshmi ! Srinivasa ! Thou art verily the ocean for all auspicious and blemishless qualities of goodness! Thou art One and the only bridge to cross the Ocean of Samsara! Thy real glory can be experienced only through (the study of) Vedanta and Upanishads! Oh! Bhakta Bhogya ! Sri Venkatachalapati! Awake! 
२९. इत्थं वृषाचलपतेरिह सुप्रभातम् ये मानवाः प्रतिदिनं पठितुं प्रवृत्ताः । 
तेषां प्रभातसमये स्मृतिरङ्गभाजां प्रज्ञां परार्थसुलभां परमां प्रसूते ॥ Those reciting these Suprabhatam slokas with Bhakti in the dawn every day will be blessed with 'Prajna' which will finally lead them to Moksha! 
CHAPTER VIII 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
Of the various Puranas in existence, 18 puranas are considered to be more sacred as Vyasokta Puranas or Puranas composed by the venerable sage Veda Vyasa. They are the Matsya, Markendeya, Bhagavata, Bhavishya, Brahma, Brahmanda, Brahmakaivastha, Vamana, Vayu, Vishnu, Varaha, Agni, Narada, Padma, Linga, Garuda, Kurma and Skanda Puranas. The stalamahatmyam of the temple of the Lord of Tirumalai, also called the Sri Venkatachala Mahatmyam, is mentioned in several Puranas such as Sri Varaha, Padma, Garuda, Brahma, Markandeya, Vamana, Brahmottara, Kanda, Aditya and Bhavishyottara Puranas. Of these the more important Puranas giving legends of the Lord of Tirumalai are the Varaha Puranam and Bha- vishyottara Puranam. It shall be our endeavour in this Chapter to make a brief study of the legends mentioned in the various Puranas. 
Part A of this Chapter deals with the legends from Varaha Puranam; Part B gives the legends from the Bhavi- shyottara Puranam, while Part C gives important legends from other Puranams. 
Part A:-Sri Venkatachala Mahatmyam in the Varaha Puranam starts with the following invocatory slokas to the Lord of Tirumalai. 
श्रियः कान्ताय कल्याणनिधये निधयेऽथिनाम् । श्रीवेङ्कटनिवासाय श्रीनिवासाय मंङ्गलम् ॥ 
Oh! Lord of Lakshmi, and Treasure House of all auspi- cious things and who art a veritable Nidhi for thy devotees, 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
119 
Thou residest on the Sri Venkata hill, Mangalam (all good auspices) to Thee Oh! Srinivasa! 
The sage Suta was once requested by Sownaka and others to enlighten them on Vishnu Kshetrams. Which was the holiest of holy Vishnu Kshetrams? And which was the Kshetram dearest to Vishnu? The sage then gladly imparted his knowledge to them as follows:- 
The Vengadam or the Venkata hill is the holiest of Vishnu Kshetrams in India. It is one that bestows all sid- dhis and all Iyswaryams on mankind. This hill called Sesha- chalam is a Varaha-Bhumi or a place holy to Lord Vishnu in his Avatar of the white boar. At the time of the Pralayam or the primeval flood, the entire universe was submerged under water. At that time Vatapatrasayi Sri Maha Vishnu took the shape of a white boar to rescue the earth from the waters of the flood. The demon Hiranyaksha however op- posed him in this and Lord Vishnu destroyed him. Earth was preserved and Vishnu commanded Brahma to recreate life on earth. Lord Vishnu then decided to reside on earth for some time in preference to his ever-joy-giving Vaikun- tam. The area south of river Gomati and near the river Suvarna Mukhi was then chosen. To this land, Garuda then brought Narayanagiri, Lord Vishnu's Kridasailam or sporting hill on his wings, and placed it on the spot chosen by the Lord. The holy hill was three yojanas long with a base of equal length and had the shape of Sesha, the thousand-headed snake. It was full of flowers and fruit- bearing trees, had a sikharam of gold and was teeming with various kinds of singing birds. The kinnaras sang and danced on it. It was verily Paradise brought on earth! Lord Vishnu in the shape of the Holy White Boar made this hill his home, occupying a Vimana on the western side of the holy Swami Pushkarini. Within a short time Lord Srinivasa 
120 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
with Conch, Sudarsana Chakra and the Mace, manifested himself in his Divya Vimana on the southern bank of the aforementioned Swami Pushkarini. Vishnu in the Boar form was then worshipped by Brahma, Rudra and other celestials. They requested him to stay on earth and bless and protect them for ever. Lord Vishnu agreed and declared that he would stay on Venkatadri and grant the wishes of his devotees. 
Lord Vishnu's Kridadri is known by several other names. It has been variously called Chintamani, Gnanadri, Teertha- dri, Pushkaradri, Vrishadri, Kanakadri, Narayanadri, Vai- kuntadri, Simhachalam, Anjanadri, Varahagiri and Nilagiri. It is hailed by the name Vrishadri in commemoration of the tapas performed by Yama Dharma Raja on the hill. It is also hailed as Venkatadri; the sound ('Vem') is an amrita bijakshara : (Kataha) stands for fortune or Iyswaryam. As the hill bestows amritaiswaryams, it is aptly called Ven- katadri. It is variously called Srinivasa Giri, Anandadri and Srisailam. 
Once Sri Rama on his way to Lanka with his monkey army was camping near the Lord's hill-Seshachalam. Anjana Devi, the mother of Anjaneya, then beseeched him to accept her hospitality on the Venkata hill. Sri Rama agreed. He and his monkey armies camped on Venkatachalam on the banks of the Swami Pushkarini. Sri Rama received the worship of Anjana Devi near the Akasa Ganga Thirtham, and bathed in the Swami Pushkarini along with Lakshmana and his followers. Sri Rama and his followers stayed on the hill in hermitages specially erected for them. One day the monkey heroes Gaksha, Gavaksha, Gavaya, Sharabha, Gan- dhamadhana in the retinue of Sri Rama's army decided to reconnoitre and investigate a cave which they discovered on the Venkata hill. This cave was the famous cave of Vai-LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
121 
kuntam. The monkey heroes cautiously entered the cave and the cave led them to a magnificent city inside. They found that words could not describe the glory of the golden city within. The people in the city were all celestial person- ages with four arms and sported ayudhas such as the chakra and the sankha. In the middle of the city was a Vimana. It was gem-studded, shone like the midday Sun and was com- parable to the Mountain Meru. It was an architectural 
beauty. A noble personage was seated in the Vimana. His face resembled that of the full moon. He had four arms. He wore the chakra and the sankha. He was seated on a gold- en throne, and had a crown studded with precious gems. His consorts Sri Devi and Bhudevi were seated by his side. On his chest shone the glorious Srivatsa and Kaustubha jewels. The monkey heroes were astonished to see such a Divya Manohara Murthi. While they were lost in admiration of the vision of the Lord, some of the celestials chased them out of the cave. They came out but tried to locate the Vaikunta cave again with the assistance of their colleagues, but did not succeed. The Vaikunta cave is unattainable and invisible even for yogis with merit. Even the celestials cannot hope to enter it without the Lord's grace. The monkeys how- ever in Sri Rama's retinue were able to enter it and see the Lord. Verily it is the Lord's play or leela! 
The daityas, Ravana and others, were then persecuting all good people in the world and harassing them. Unable to stand up to them, Jabali, Kashyapa, Gautama, Agasthya, Vamadeva, Sadananda, Shanaka, Indra and others resolved to seek the assistance of Lord Vishnu to put an end to the misdeeds of miscreants. They therefore proceeded to Sri Vaikuntam and found that Lord Sriman Narayana was on the earth at Venkatachalam. Brahma whose assistance was then sought, advised them that Ravana was a great devotee 
122 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
of the Lord, that he could be destroyed by Lord Vishnu only and not by others. Lord Vishnu was on the Venkata hill and would soon give darshan to King Dasaratha who was doing penance on the banks of Swami Pushkarini to propitiate Vishnu. Brahma and others therefore went to Venkatadri to obtain darshan of the Lord of Tirumalai. 
King Dasaratha who was given mantropadesham by his Preceptor Vasishta was at Tirumalai. He bathed in the Swami Pushkarini and sat in nishta reciting the Venkatesa Ashtakshari mantra. Brahma and the celestials also prayed to the Lord to obtain his darshan, when lo! there was great illumination and the Lord of Tirumalai revealed Himself to his assembled devotees in a Vimana. It was verily a celestial Vimana with several gopurams and avaranams. The. Vimana had several doors of gold; the doorsteps of the holy residence were decorated with sapphires, emeralds, rubies and other precious gems. It had gopurams with kalasams or vessels of glittering gold. It had several beautiful and architectually perfect thousand-pillared mantapams; several vahanams such as chariots, horses, elephants, were in it. Such an auspicious Vimana had never been seen before by mortal eyes. Brahma and the others entered the Vimana to have darshan of the Lord. Siva and others also arrived there post-haste to worship the Lord. The sage Agastya and others then sang the eulogies of the Lord. 
नमस्ते यज्ञरूपाय यज्ञभोक्त्रे नमो नमः । 
यज्ञकर्ते नमो यज्ञप्रियाय च नमो नमः । 
Salutation to thee who art the Roopa of Yagna (embodi- ment of the sacrificial rites) and the receiver of the Yagna- phalam or the fruit of Yagna (one who enjoys the Yagna- phala). Salutation, to thee again and again. Thou art the Supreme Spirit of Yagna! Salutation to thee who art fond 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
123 
of Yagnas! Our respectful obeisance to thee again and again. 
Indra then commenced his stotram with the slokas: 
ओं नमो वेङ्कटेशाय शेषाद्रिनिलयाय च । सिंहाचलनिवासाय श्रीमन्नारायणाय च ॥ 
'Om Namo Venkatesaya' is the Sri Venkatesa Ash- takshari mantra. Salutation to Lord Venkatesa, resident of the Seshadri Hill. Salutation to Sriman Narayana, resi- dent of the Simhachala Hill. 
Saunaka, Dasaratha and others praised the Lord. Brahma then sang the praises of the Lord and prayed for His protec- tion when the Lord replied "O! Kamalasana! Fear not, I shall protect." 
अहमेव गतिर्ब्रह्मन् ! भवतां माऽस्तु तद्भयम् । 
अभयं भवतां दत्तं मया हि कमलासन ! ॥ 
"In a short time, I shall certainly destroy the cruel Ravana who is a thorn to the universe (a source of vexation to the universe or foe to the universe) along with his relations and retinue." Sanaka and others then prayed to the Lord that He should not be invisible on Venkatachala but must be visible to one and all. The Lord granted this boon and assured Indra that Ravana would be killed soon. The Lord then heard Shankara's request that he should be wherever the Lord Himself is and agreed to this by saying 'I shall stay on Venkatadri until the end of this Kalpa. You shall also stay near this hill'. Dasaratha was then ordained to perform a Yagna in Ayodhya and informed that he would be blessed with four powerful and brave sons. While the others left the Vimana, taking leave of the Lord, Brahma remained. He was then asked 'why standest thou here, what is thy de- sire?' Brahma then replied: Oh! Lord of the Venkata Hill! Hear and grant me my wish. In the Kaliyuga, people cannot perform tapas and thus deserve thy grace. They 
124 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
will be weak in body, diseased, lusty by nature and sinners in general. If you are not kind to them, their fate will be the eternal fires of Naraka or Hell. Hence my prayer that thou should manifest Thyself here in Kaliyuga, give them darshan and save them'. And the Lord replied 'I shall do even so. I shall remain on this hill with Sridevi and Bhudevi, granting freely the wishes of my devotees. The tapas, yagnas and yoga done on this hill shall achieve easy results. The Pushkarini on my hill shall be the Swami Pushkarini. The desires of those who bathe in this shall be fulfilled. Those who wor- ship me after a holy bath in this Pushkarini shall have their desires fulfilled without fail!' 
The Lord then destroyed the cruel Rakshasas on the Venkata hill region by using his Sudarshana chakra, and also agreed to the performance of his Brahmotsavam on the Venkata hill. 
The Varaha Puranam also mentions the leelas of the Lord Venkateswara in Kaliyuga. He will be a mouni (main- tain silence) in Kaliyuga, and be visible to earthly beings in the archa form. The celestial Vimana from Vaikuntam will be invisible. The Lord of Tirumalai will also be sporting with his consort Lakshmi on the hill. He will continue to be worshipped by the celestials invisible to mortal eyes. The Lord will bestow his blessings on all who seek His grace or think of Him or go on a pilgrimage to the Venkata hill. 
"Venkatesa Samo Devo Nasthi Nasthi Maheetale." None equals Lord Venkateswara--not one--none equals Lord Venkateswara in the entire Universe. 
The Varaha Puranam also mentions several other legends showing the leela of Lord Venkateswara. One such is the story of an old Brahmin who was crying out for the assis- tance of his son Koundinya on the Venkata hill. The Lord Himself then assumed the garb of a youth and taking the 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
125 
Brahmin by hand took him near a spring of water and or- dained him to bathe in the waters of that spring. Lo! the hundred-year-old helpless Brahmin was transformed into a youth! From then onwards, the spring got the name Kumara Dhara. In another instance, the Lord assisted Sankana, a ruler of the lunar dynasty, who had lost his kingdom and was bemoaning his misfortune on the banks of a lake near the river Suvarna Mukhi. A celestial voice ordained him to go on a pilgrimage to Tirumalai and worship the Lord there for six months taking a daily bath in the Swami Pushkarini. The king followed the instructions of his celestial guide, obtained the grace of the Lord of Tirumalai and regained his kingdom. 
Another legend in the Varaha Puranam mentions of a poor Brahmin going by the name of Atma Rama. He bathed in the Kapila Thirtham and made a pilgrimage to Venka- tachalam. A yogi on the Venkata hill initiated him by giv- ing him mantropadesham and instructed him that he should worship Maha Lakshmi. Atma Rama reciting the mantra took a dip in the holy Pushkarini and obtained the grace of the Lord of Tirumalai. 
The Varaha Puranam mentions of seventeen thirthams or springs of water in the Venkatachalam hill area. They include the Swami Pushkarini, Kumara Dhara, Tumburu, Akasha Ganga, Pandava, Papanashanam, Deva, Jabali, Palguni, Kapila, Chakra, Panchayudha, Agni, Brahma, Vishvaksena thirthams etc. The Varaha Puranam mentions that holy baths on certain days in these thirthams will give special results such as papavimochanam, happiness and pros- perity on earth and Moksha after death. 
Another legend concerns Vasuvu, a gardener. Vasuvu and his son Veera were in the habit of cooking 'tandulams' and offering the cooked food as naivedyam to the Lord 
126 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
along with honey. One day Vasuvu went to the forest to obtain honey for the Lord's naivedyam. On his return he found that his son had taken his daily meal. Vasuvu got angry that his son had misbehaved and he attempted to do away with him, when the Lord of Tirumalai appeared to him and prevented him from killing his son. The Lord explained to the Nishada that his son had already fed him and that he was a great devotee. One other legend concerns the Vishnu Bhakta, Rangadasa. Rangadasa originally belonged to the city of Narayanapuri in Pandya Desa. The Lord graced him by giving him darshan. This Rangadasa then dug a well for the Lord in Venkatadri. On one day, some Gan- dharvas were sporting themselves in the well constructed by him. Rangadasa who had gone there to gather flowers for the Lord was enchanted by the sight of the Gandharvas and was late for the mala-kainkaryam in the temple. The temple priest chastised him for being late. Rangadasa was shy because of the apachara done to the Lord, but the ever gracious Lord gave him darshan. He was informed that he-Rangadasa would be reborn as a king. He would then be a vaishnava bhaktha and construct a Vimanam and a prakaram for the Lord of Tirumalai. Another important legend concerns king Tondaman who was the son of Suveera and Nandinidevi. On one day observing a multicoloured parrot the King chased it. It took him to Venkatachalam. A nishada on the Venkata Hill informed him that the parrot belonged to Lord Srinivasa. King Tondaman then express- ed that he very much desired to have darshan of Lord Srinivasa. The nishada led him to Swami Pushkarini. The king bathed in the Swami Pushkarini and had darshan of the Lord of Tirumalai under a tree. Another legend mentions of a nishada by name Vasuvu who chased a white boar which was destroying every day the crops grown by 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
127 
him on Venkatachalam. One day the chased white boar led Vasuvu to an ant-hill. The boar entered the ant-hill. The angry nishada tried to dig up the ant-hill to trap and kill the boar, but fell unconscious! The nishada and his son were however soon enlightened that the white boar was no other than Lord Vishnu and that the ant-hill should be flooded with milk from a black-coloured cow when the Lord would manifest himself in Venkatachalam in the archa form. Tondaman was from then onwards to arrange for his worship. The nishada went to the king and informed him about the Lord in the ant-hill. Tondaman followed the nishada, flooded the ant-hill and discovered the Lord's archa form in the ant-hill. He then constructed the temple for the Lord of Tirumalai. There were two trees in the temple area; one was a tamarind tree and the other a cham- paka tree. The Lord informed him that the tamarind tree was sacred to him and that the champaka tree was sacred to Lakshmi. Tondaman also constructed a prakaram for the temple. 
II 
Legends from Bhavishyottara Puranam:-The hill Venkatachalam was called Vrishachalam in Kritayuga, Anjanadri in Tretayuga, and Seshachalam in Dwaparayuga. In Kaliyuga, it bears the name of Venkatachalam. A Rakshasa by name Vrishasura was persecuting Rishis and the people in the area in Kritayuga. He was a devotee of Lord Narasimha and had obtained a boon from him that Vishnu would give him battle as desired by him. Lord Vishnu therefore fought with the demon and killed him with his Sudarshana Chakra. Vrishasura then prayed to the Lord that the hill should bear his name. Hence the name Vrishachalam. The hill is called Anjanachalam as Anjanadevi, the mother of Anjaneya, performed tapas on it. 
128 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
It also bears the name of Seshasailam in honour of the thousand-headed Sesha. It bears the name of Venkata- chalam as it is a hill which burns away all sins. The con- nected legend is as follows: A Brahmin by name Madhava belonging to Kalahasti fell in love with a vyabhichari or a prostitute and lived with her against all the canons of ac- cepted Vedic religion. He became a great sinner, eating meat, and drinking prohibited liquor. After some time his mate died and Madhava followed a party of pilgrims bound for Venkatadri. All his sins were instantaneously burnt away on his coming into contact with the sacred hill of Lord Vishnu. Brahma who then gave darshan to Madhava informed him that Madhava would be reborn as Akasha Raja and rule the whole of Tondamandalam with Narayanapuri as his capital, that the holy mother would be born as his daughter and that Lord Vishnu would then wed her. Brahma also named the hill Venkatadri in com- memoration of its powers of burning away all kinds of sins. 
Srinivasa Kalyanam with Sri Padmavati:-Long long ago Kasyapa and others were performing a yagna on the banks of the River Jahnavi. A doubt then arose among them about the proper Yagnapurusha who deserved the Yagnaphalam. The sages were not in a position to decide which of the Devas deserved the honour of the Yagnapha- lam. Sage Bhrigu was therefore enjoined by the assembly of rishis to resolve the issue. Bhrigu agreed and decided to test and proclaim the One that deserved the worship of Mankind and left for Brahma Loka. Brahma was then adjudged by him to be an Apujya, that is, one who does not deserve worship. He then proceeded to Kailasam and found the Lord sporting with his consort Parvati. Bhrigu therefore decided that he also was unfit for the honour contemplated and left for Vaikuntam, the residence of Lord 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
129 
Vishnu. Here the Lord Sriman Narayana was reclining on the Sesha and Lakshmi was by his side. Bhrigu was brutal in his behaviour1 to the Lord, but the Lord was kind and solicitous about the welfare of the sage. The sage therefore decided: 
हरिः सर्वोत्तमः साक्षाद्रमा देवी तदन्तरा । 
Hari was the uttama Daivatham and his consort Ramaa Devi deserved worship after Him. 
Lakshmi however was put out with the Lord and left for Karaveera Kshetram on earth, leaving her Lord in grief. And the Lord poring over ways and means to pacify Lakshmi, left for Venkatadri on earth. On this hill was the Holy Pushkarini and on the banks of the Pushkarini, a tamarind tree. Lord Vishnu's tejas or divine shakti mani- fested itself in an ant-hill under the tamarind tree mentioned above. 
A thousand years flew by. It was the end of Dwapara- yuga and the Chola kingdom in India was being ruled by a kindly ruler, full of merit. Brahma then took the shape of a cow and Rudra that of a calf. Lakshmi then became a milk-maid and sold the cow and the calf to the Chola king. The celestial cow then found its way to the ant-hill on Venkatachalam where the Lord had taken refuge. The cow emptied its milk on the ant-hill, enabling Lord Srinivasa to drink up the nourishing food. The cow got into the habit of nourishing the Lord thus every day. The cowherd 
1. The sage had kicked the Lord on the chest-the abode of 
Lakshmi. And instead of punishing the sage, the Lord had said to him: 
S.V.-6 
वज्रष्टगुणां विद्धि मच्छरीरे कठोरताम् । 
किमर्थं ताडितं विप्र ! कोमलाङघितलेन तत् ॥ पादौ ते कोमलौ दिव्यौ मच्छरीरसमागमात् । कियदुखं समापन्नौ न जानामि द्विजोत्तम ॥ 
130 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
in charge of the King's cattle noticed the loss of milk, fol- lowed the cow one day and threw his stick at the cow to chastise it. The Lord however received the blow and saved the cow. The cowherd died immediately and the Chola king who arrived later at Venkatachalam to investigate was cursed and became a Pisacham (spirit). On the King's prayer Lord Srinivasa informed him that he would be released from the curse soon, that he would then be reborn as Akasa Raja and that he would gain merit by giving his daughter Padmavati in marriage to him. Akasa Raja would also then present a gem-studded crown of gold to him which he would wear on the evening of every Friday. 
Srinivasa then obtained from Vishnu in the Boar form his consent to stay on Venkatachalam. In return Srinivasa promised that Lord Varaha would thenceforth receive the 'Prathama Darshanam' and 'Prathama Naivedyam' of Venkatachalam. The Lord Vishnu in the Boar form placed the services of his 'Sevika' Vakula Malika at the dis- posal of Srinivasa. Vakula Malika, who was no other than Yasodha Devi of the Krishna Avatar days, who had been promised by the Lord that she would see Him as a Kalyanamurthi in the Kali yuga, looked after Srinivasa as a mother would look after her own child. 
At the end of Dwaparayuga and after the great Maha- bharatha war, Tonda Desa was being ruled in plenty and prosperity by King Akasa Raja. He had no children. On the advice of his preceptors, he therefore determined to perform a Yagna to beget children. For this purpose, the sacrificial land was being ploughed when lo! a thousand- petalled lotus was discovered in the Yagnavatika. In the lotus was a baby. She was Beauty personified and was no other than an amsa of Sri Lakshmi, born to wed Lord Srinivasa. The king and his queen Dharuni Devi wereLEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
131 
happy that the Lord had blessed them thus with a daughter. A celestial voice then told them "Oh! king! She is thy daughter. Protect her. She will get immortal fame". The precious infant was named Padmavati, as she was found in a Padma or lotus. 
The foundling child soon grew up into a very beautiful young girl. One day the sage Narada appeared to her as an old 'tapasvi' in the royal presence, read her palm and predicted that she would be the chosen bride of Lord Vishnu. That very day the bridegroom Srinivasa was hunting in the Venkatachalam forests. During his sport, he espied a wild elephant and pursued it to the royal plea- sure-gardens where Padmavati and her friends were playing with each other. Here the Jagatpita (the Father of the Universe) saw the Jaganmatha (Mother of the Universe); and the Holy Mother saw her future Lord. Lord Srinivasa then announced himself to his bride as follows: "My father is Vasudeva. My mother is Devaki. Balaram is my bro- ther. Subhadra is my sister. Arjuna is my friend. The Pandavas are my relations. I was born on the Ashtami day in the Krishna Paksha; my bodily colour is Krishna (or dark). Hence I am called Krishna". Padmavati then replied to his queries with becoming shyness and dignity. "I am the daughter of Sri Akasa Raja. My name is Pad- mavati". Lord Srinivasa fell in love with the maiden and ex- pressed his desire to wed her immediately, but he was forced to retreat and return home. He then declared his passion for the maiden Padmavati to Vakula Malika, his foster mother. The Lord also enlightened her about Padmavati's past birth as follows: "In Tretayuga, I was no other than Sri Rama, son of King Dasaratha. Along with Sita and Lakshmana, I then left for the forests of Dandaka. While we were away, Ravana attempted to carry away Sita! Listen 
132 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
Oh! Vakula Malika! Agni Deva then came to the rescue of Sita. He confronted Ravana, and convinced him with sweet words that the real Sita was with him in Agniloka. Agni then managed to exchange and replace the real Sita by one Vedavati disguised as the real Sita. The real Sita was safely lodged with Svaha Devi, the consort of Agni The Maya Sita however was taken away to Lanka by the demon Ravana. This Maya Sita was no other than the Vedavati who had immolated herself in Agni, when Ravana attempted to molest her in her previous birth. Vedavati had then made a solemn oath and announced that she would be the cause of the destruction of Ravana and his tribe. After the destruction of Ravana, the real Sita was restored to Me during the Agnipariksha of the Maya Sita. The very compassionate Sita then prayed to me that I should wed the Maya Sita. I granted Sita's boon saying that it would be fulfiilled in Dwaparayuga when I would assume the form of Lord Srinivasa. The time for the fulfilment of that boon has come. Padmavati is no other than Vedavati of that Trethayuga". Vakula Malika who heard the story of Padmavati from the lips of Srinivasa was glad in her heart as she desired to see her Srinivasa as a Kalyana Murthi. She therefore promised Lord Srinivasa that she would pro- ceed to Akasa Raja's city and fix up the holy marriage 
alliance. 
Vakula Devi then quickly mounted a horse, crossed the river Suvarna Mukhi and reached the Holy Siva temple near sage Agastya's hermitage. Here she learnt from Akasa Raja's retinue that Padmavati had met a handsome young man in the royal pleasure gardens, that Padmavati loved the youth and fell unconscious after departure. Akasa Raja's Guru, Brihaspati, advised the King that Lord Siva should be pro- pitiated by an abhishekam and they were therefore worship- 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
133 
ping Lord Siva as commanded by the King. Vakula then announced herself as a Harisevika and requested that the friends of Padmavati should arrange an audience for her with Queen Dharunidevi. After the abhishekam, Vakula was taken to the city and admitted into the audience hall of Queen Dharunidevi. Meanwhile Srinivasa who was anxious regarding the outcome of his envoy, himself donned the robe of a Pulinda sooth-sayer, and proceeded to Naraya- napuram. Srinivasa was then in the garb of a toothless hill-woman and had a big paunch, big ears and wore a neck- lace of shells. She had a seven month old baby tied to her back in her saree and a big bamboo basket of grain on her head. Sporting a stick in her hand, she entered the city of Narayanapuram and went on shouting that she would pre- dict the future and protect husbands, sons and relations. This is beautifully described in the following slokas of the Bhavishyottara Puranam: 
वेणुगुल्यं स्वशिरसि दधाना धन्यपूरितम् । लम्बोदरी लम्बकर्णलम्बतार्धपयोधरा ॥ अदन्त इष्कवदना तदाऽयूद्धर्मदेवता । ब्रह्माण नाभिसञ्जातं सप्रमासवयोयुतम् ॥ रुदन्तं रुष्कवदनं कृशाङ्गी दीर्घबाहुकम् । शिशुं बद्ध्वा चीरवस्त्रे नृत्यन्ती जदगदीश्वरी ॥ यष्ट घृत्वा करे याऽगात् सबाला धर्मदेवता नारायणपुरं प्राप्ता नारदाब्जजवन्दिता ॥ 
पुरीं समागत्य जगर्ज चेत्थं 
पतीन् सुतान् बन्धुगणान् ददामि । 
श्रुत्वा वचस्तद्रदितं पुराङ्गनाः 
ऊचस्तदार्तां नृपवल्लभां प्रति ॥ 
The Pulinda woman then informed queen Dharunidevi as follows:—“Devi, Narayanaswamy is my husband. This baby is my son. I have come here to tell you everything 
134 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
about the past, the present and the future". Dharunidevi then gave her the required presents along with scented betel leaves and nuts. The Pulinda woman with her baby on her lap then told the Queen in a sing-song voice as follows: "Yesterday a handsome young man dressed as a kiratha mounted on a horse was seen by your Padmavati; she is in love with Him and desires Him. She desires to wed the Lord of Tirumalai, Sri Srinivasa. Yesterday's hunter is no other than Srinivasa. It will be well for thee to give Padmavati in marriage to Srinivasa who is 
'वैकुण्ठस्थो हरिः साक्षात् वर्तते वेङ्कटालये । 'श्रीनिवास' इति ख्यातो विद्यावान् धनवान् बली ॥ 
If you fail to heed to my words, Padmavati will collapse within three days. In proof of what I say, an old woman will come within an hour to broach the subject of alliance bet- ween Padmavati and Srinivasa". The Pulinda woman then left taking leave from queen Dharunidevi. Padmavati then confirmed the story of her tryst with Srinivasa. As correctly predicted by the Pulinda woman, Vakuladevi herself approached Dharunidevi within the appointed time and asked for the hand of Padmavati for Srinivasa. Dharuni- devi and Akasa Raja then counselled with each other and declared their approval of the proposed alliance. Akasa Raja then sent for Brihaspati and Suka Muni to fix up the Kalyana lagnam. Suka Muni advised Akasa Raja that they would all become blessed by making Kanyadanam to Lord Srinivasa. Brihaspati then examined the nadikutams and yonikutams of the future couple taking into considera- tion the birth-stars of Srinivasa and Padmavati (Sravanam and Mrigasirsha respectively). He declared happily that the planets were all auspicious and that the wedding bet- ween the two would be auspicious, and result in happiness for the couple and the world. Akasa Raja therefore sent a 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
135 
Kalyana-patrika to Srinivasa through Suka Muni fixing the Kanyalagnam on Vaisakha Sukla Dasami (Thursday). Srini- vasa then received the Kalyana-patrika and signified his con- sent to marry Padmavati. Vakuladevi also returned from Narayanapuram and declared the happy news of her em- bassy to Lord Srinivasa. Brahma, Siva, Kubera, Kasyapa. Bharadwaja, Vamadeva, Gautama, Viswamitra, Vasishta, Valmiki, Parasurama, Pulasthya, Dadhichi and other sages soon arrived on Venkatachalam to witness the marriage of the Lord of Tirumalai. The divine architect Viswakarma then built a glorious city on Venkatachalam. Indra along with Maya then proceeded to Narayanapuram and construct- ed a beautiful Kalyanamantapam there. 
Srinivasa then said unto himself "I can never be happy without Ramaa Devi. Lakshmi has been with me even when I was a Vatapatrasayi on the ocean of milk". Lord Srini- vasa then directed the Sun God to proceed to Karavira- puram and to invite the Lord's consort to Venkatachalam. The Sun God conveyed the Lord's message to her that the Lord had become an Asakta and was pining for Lakshmi. Lakshmi therefore in anxiety that her Lord was in danger rushed immediately to Venkatachalam. She worshipped her Lord and embraced him; the divine couple were thus united and Srinivasa really became Sri Srinivasa or Lord Srinivasa. Then Lord Srinivasa said to her "Oh! Sitadevi! Remember thy request made to me in the Rama Avatara period, when thou sought a boon from me that I should wed Vedavati, the Maya Sita. The time to fulfil that boon had come". Sri Lakshmi remembered her request in Treta- yuga and prayed to the Lord to marry Vedavati. Lord Srinivasa was then given a holy bath by Sri Lakshmi herself. He also worshipped the 'Sami' tree near the Kumara Dhara thirtham, obtained a loan from Kubera on the understanding 
136 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
that his debt would be repaid within a thousand years and proceeded with all his divine retinue and paraphernalia to marry Sri Padmavati. Akasa Raja then presented a gold crown studded with gems and several other valuable orna- ments to Lord Srinivasa. The marriage was then performed according to holy Vedic rites and Lord Srinivasa tied the mangala-sutram and Sri Padmavati became his consort. The celestials then rained flowers on the Holy Couple. 
III 
Several other Puranas also repeat many of the legends mentioned in the Varaha and Bhavishyottara Puranas. The Padma Puranam narrates the legend connected with the des- truction of the demons Madhu and Kaitabha. These demons were extremely powerful and could not be overpowered by the celestials including Vishnu. The Lord therefore cleverly obtained a boon from them that they would both die in his hands. The demons then prayed to him that He should kill them on a spot where there was no water. Lord Vishnu then enlarged his thighs, seated the demons on his thigh and destroyed them, with his chakra. To this day, the Lord of Tirumalai is worshipped as Madhukaitabhari, that is, the destroyer of the demons Madhu and Kaitabha. 
The Padma Puranam also mentions the story of Bhrigu insulting Lord Vishnu, Vishnu coming down to earth on Tirupati and his being discovered by King Tondaman. 
According to the Brahmanda Puranam, the Lord of Tirumalai is Lord Krishna who fed himself with the milk from the breasts of Putana, a female demon and then des- troyed her. He is worshipped in the 'Sri Venkateswara Sa- hasranamavali' as Vasudeva and as One who delights in eating Navanita or butter. He is the One who delivered the 
LEGENDS OF THE LORD OF TIRUMALAI 
137 
celestials Nalakubara and Manigriva from the curse of the sage Narada. The legend connected with the above is nar- rated in the Brahma Vaivarta Purana. Other names of Vish- nu such as Nandagopa Manohara, Brindaranya Nivasaka, Gopanganachelachoraya, Kaliyaphani darpagna, Rāsakrida- parayana, Rukmini Nayanotsava, and the connected legends described in the Brahma Vaivarta Purana and the Bhagavata indicate to us that the Lord of Tirumalai is no other than Lord Krishna. Similarly, Vishnu names such as Kausalya- tanaya, Dasakanta Sirodhvamsi, etc. in the Brahmanda Pura- na show that Lord Srinivasa is no other than Sri Rama. The connected legends are too well known to need repetition. 
Shri J.H. Dave mentions a particularly interesting legend regarding the Swami Pushkarini from the Skanda. This legend is reproduced below: 
"Skanda records this story of Dharmagupta, son of King Nanda. The latter in his old age adopted an ascetic life and left the kingdom to his son Dharmagupta. Once, this Dharmagupta while hunting spent some time in a forest at night. A lion pursued him; so the king climbed up a tree. A bear also resorted to the same tree out of the fear of the lion who was sitting below, waiting to catch the prey. The king and the bear agreed to remain awake in turn, each for half the night and permit the other to sleep. First, the king slept and the bear protected him, remaining wakeful. In spite of the lion's entreaties to drop the king, the bear remained faithful to its promise to the king. After mid- night it was the king's turn to watch over the sleeping bear. On the lion's entreaties, the faithless king dropped down the bear as prey to the lion." The bear woke up, assumed the form of a yaksha and cursed the king to turn mad as the penalty for his heinous and criminal breach of trust. His re- tired father, Nanda, was informed of this. Ultimately, they 
138 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
discovered the Swami Pushkarini lake and after a bath in it, it is said, Dharmagupta was cured of his madness.1 
A pilgrimage to Venkatachala and a bath in Swami Pushkarini also cured sage Kasyapa of his evil. Even though he had remedies to cure king Parikshit of the serpent-bite of Takshaka, he did not go to cure him and on being bribed by Takshaka with jewels, he returned home from mid-way and Parikshit died of the serpent-bite. Any one who has remedies must cure the sick and the injured till the last moment. 
The legendary accounts given above while not exhaus- tive give us only an idea of the glory of Sri Venkateswara of Venkatachala. Words or legends can never adequately des- cribe the glory or grace of the Lord, which has to be ex- perienced to be really enjoyed. 
1. Immortal India, Vol. I. by J. H. Dave, published by Bharatiya 
Vidya Bhavan, Bombay, pp. 179 to 181. 
CHAPTER IX 
FESTIVALS, DAILY WORSHIP AND SOME PECULIAR CUSTOMS IN THE TEMPLE 
It has already been indicated that Tirumalai or Venga- dam was famous in the olden days for its festivals conducted on the hill. These festivals continue to this day, giving it fame, splendour and the enviable reputation that the temple has every day the radiant glory of 'Paccha Toranams and Nitya Kalyanams'. Among the several festivals conducted on the hill, the Brahmotsavam is the most popular festival drawing huge crowds to the temple. 
Brahmotsavam festival:-This festival bears the name of Brahmotsavam as the very first Utsavam for the Lord of Tirumalai in the temple is said to have been conducted by Brahma, the Lord of Creation (Varaha Puranam, Chapter 50). The Brahmotsavam is a festival which is conducted according to the Sastras. 
Prior to 966 A.D. only one Brahmotsavam was con- ducted in Tirumalai. In 966 A.D. the Pallava Queen Samavai, who arranged for the installation of the Bhoga Srinivasa image in the temple, made arrangements for two Brahmotsavam festivals, one in the Purattasi month (on the day of the Chitra star) and another during the Mukkoti Dvadasi period. Thus, two Brahmotsavams came to be performed even in the 10th century. Other royal bene- factors who worshipped the Lord in the temple were not slow in following the example set up by Samavai, and it is no wonder there was a proliferation of the Brahmotsavam festi- 
1. (Telugu) Green Toranams or decorations made with mango leaves etc. for festive occasions. Nitya Kalyanam stands for auspiciousness and auspicious ceremonies conducted everyday -such as the Kalyana Utsavam of the Lord. 
140 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
val in Tirumalai in the centuries that followed, as the following inscription1 found on the north wall of the third prakara in Tirumalai temple will show: 
"May there be prosperity, Hail! 1 atirasa-padi on the day of Yugadi (Chandra-Sam- vatsaradi) festival (Telugu New Year's day) and

thus making a total of 250 atirasa-padi to be presented along with 250 palams of chandanam, 1,200 areca-nuts, 25,000 betels and 250 pana-weight of refined camphor yearly on the 250 days of Tirukkodi-tirunal (Brahmotsavam), Tin- gal-divasam (monthly festival days) and Visesha-divasam (special festival days) celebrated in Tirumalai temple...." 
The inscription is dated 8-7-1551, and gives a list of Brahmotsavams current in the temple at that time. It is obvious that there were at least eleven Brahmotsavams at that time. Besides the above, several other festivals such as Sri Jayanthi, Uri-adi, Dipavali, Yugadi (Telugu New Year's day), Sri Rama Navami etc. were conducted in the temple. The inscription clearly informs us that festi- vals including the Brahmotsavams, Tingaldivasam (month- ly festivals) and Visesha-divasam (special festivals) took place for 250 days in a year. 
At present, the temple conducts four Brahmotsavam festivals a year; the first in the Purattasi month, the second on Ratha Saptami day, the third on Kausika Dvadasi day in Kartika month and the fourth on the Mukkoti Ekadasi day. The festivals usually take place for several days. The Utsavam during the Ratha Saptami period is considered to be an Arsha Utsavam, while the Utsavam during the Kausika Dvadasi period is considered as Rakshasa Utsavam. The 
1. The author is grateful to Shri M.A.S. Kesavachari, T.T. Devasthanam Agama Pandit, for furnishing some particulars about the Brahmotsavams conducted at present in the temple. The author himself has first hand knowledge of the Garudotsa- vam, and other Utsavams. 
FESTIVALS AND PECULIAR CUSTOMS IN THE TEMPLE 143 
most important of these Utsavams conducted at present is Brahmotsavam in the Purattasi month (September-October) which is an Utsavam performed by Manavas or men of the earth. This Utsavam commences on the day when the Sra- vana Nakshatram or star is prominent. On the day before the Sravana star day (thithi), Ankurarpanam is done by sowing 'navadhanya' seeds for germination in specially de- corated new pots called 'Palikas'. This is supposed to form part of the propitiatory offerings to the Nityasuris or celes- tials in the temple. A 'Poorna Kumbham' is also installed in the yagasala. 
The festival actually commences on the first day with the Dhvajarohanam-a ceremony in which the Lord's flag with the Garuda emblem is flown on a flag staff erected next to the Dhvajastambham. Everyday the Utsavam for the Lord is conducted with splendour, along with homas etc., as per rituals laid down. The Lord's Utsava Vigraham (with or without his consorts Sridevi and Bhudevi) is also taken in procession twice-once in the day time and again in the night time with the appropriate Vahanam. The Vahanams for the processions at night on the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth and tenth days are the Pedda Sesha, Hamsa, Simha, Punya Koti Vimanam, Garuda, Elephant, Chandra-Prabha, Aswa, Ivory Palanquin, and Tirucchi Vahanams, respectively. 
The important festival days are the fifth, eighth and eleventh days. The morning procession of the Lord on the seventh day with Surya Prabha Vahanam is also worth seeing. 
The Utsavam on the night of the fifth day is called the Garuda Seva or Garudotsavam. On this day the processional deity alone is taken in procession on the Garuda; the con- sorts of the Lord are not seated by his side on the Vahanam 
144 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
as usual.1 On this day, the Lord is given 'Uyyala Seva' in the evening.? This Uyyala Seva or 'Seva in the Swing' takes place in the open area near the Dhvajastambham. The processional deity comes out of the temple in a Tirucchi3 and the poles of the Tirucchi are fixed to chains (fixed to the ceiling) with rings attached to them and the whole Tiru- cchi is swung to and fro during the Swing or Uyyala Seva. During this Asthanam or durbar, songs are sung and Vedic hymns etc. chanted. 
The deity is then taken and installed on the Garuda vahanam. The Makarakanti ornament and the Lakshmi haram on the Mula-vigraham are then brought and used for the decoration of the Lord on the Garuda vahanam. The vahanam is then taken in procession around the east, west, north and south Mada streets of Tirumalai. The Lord has the usual paraphernalia during this procession such as Chatra, Chamara, Mangala Vadyas, recital of the holy books, etc. 
The car festival takes place on the eighth day. This 'Rathotsavam' attracts the largest crowds during the Brah- motsavam festival days. The Utsavamurthi along with the consorts is brought on to the temple car early in the morn- ing. The Lord in the temple car and the temple car are then gaily decorated; the temple chariot is then taken round the streets of Tirumalai. 
On the eleventh day of the festival, the processional deity is taken on a Tirucchi Vahanam to the Swami Push- karini. The Chakram of the Lord (also called Chakrattal- var) then gets a bath in the Swami Pushkarini. At the same 
1. T.T.D. Epigraphical Series, Vol. II, Inscription of Saluva 
Narasimha's time, pp. 27-30. 
2. Uyyala seva for the Lord is performed on all the Brahmotsa 
vam days in the evenings. 
3. A sort of open palanquin. 
FESTIVALS AND PECULIAR CUSTOMS IN THE TEMPLE 145 
time, the devotees of the Lord also plunge into the Swami Pushkarini. A bath at this time in the Swami Pushkarini is considered to be very holy and merit-giving. The Brah- motsavam comes to an end with this snana or bathing of the Lord in the Pushkarini. 
Adhyayanotsavam:-The earliest reference in the tem- ple inscriptions to the Adhyayanotsavam which is performed to this day in the temple was in the year 1400 A.D. It is an annual Vedic festival when the Vedas and the Tamil Pra- bandams are recited in the temple. This festival is con- ducted on Mukkoti Ekadasi day and is performed for about twenty days. The last day is Sattumurai day. Nammalvar's Tiruvaymoli along with the other hymns from Tamil Pra- bandam are recited during the Adhyayanotsavam. 
In the olden days the festival commenced ten days be- fore Vaikunta Ekadasi and continued for about twenty days. During this period the processional images were taken round the streets of Tirumalai when hymns from the Nala- yira Prabandam of the Alwars were recited. In the olden days, one Adhyayanotsavam was also performed in front of Sri Ramanuja for twelve days in the month of Chittirai. This followed the arrangements for the daily recital of Veda made by Sri Devaraya Maharaya in 1430 A.D. The Kalyanamantapam was utilised at this time for housing the processional deity. The Utsava vigraham, Malayappan, is to this day kept in the Kalyana Mantapam during the Brahmotsavam and Adhyayanotsavam periods. 
Pavitrotsavam:-A festival called the Pavitrotsavam was first instituted in the time of Saluva Narasimha. The relevant inscription regarding this festival is to be found on the north wall of the Vagappadi verandah in the first prakara 
146 
SRI VENKATESWARA 
of Tirumalai temple and the relevant extracts from this are given below.1 
"May there be prosperity! On Wednesday combined with (the star) Rohini, being the 10th lunar day of the bright fortnight of the Makara month in the Subhanu year, current with the Saka year 1385, the Sthanattar of Tirumalai executed the following silasasanam in favour of Sriman Mahamandalesvara Medinimisaraganda Kattari-saluva Mallayadeva Maharaja, son of Saluva Errakampayadeva Maharaja, viz., 
and for the items of expenditure to be incurred in con- nection with the celebration of the Tirupavitratirunal, in your name, for five days in the bright fortnight of the Avani month, so as to commence with the ankurarpanam sowing the nine kinds of seeds in small earthen pots on the night of the dasami (tenth lunar day), to decorate the Tirumamani- mantapam (the front mantapam adjoining the sanctum) on the Ekadasi day and then seat on the dvadasi day Malaiki- niyaninra-Perumal and Nachchimar in the Tirumamani- mantapam, after putting on the pavitram (sanctified thread round the head, neck, wrist etc.) and taking Him in proces- sion through the streets, viz.,
